2:27:1651:0:14:72:464:700:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:C:Sovereign Credit Risk and Exchange Rates: Evidence from CDS Quanto Spreads 
2:28:1725:14:14:72:334:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Patrick Augustin, Mikhail Chernov, and Dongho Song
2:29:1775:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 24506
2:30:1803:14:14:72:221:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:April 2018, Revised June 2018
2:31:1832:14:28:72:221:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. C1,E43,E44,G12,G15
2:32:1858:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:33:1866:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:Sovereign  CDS  quanto  spreads—the  difference  between  CDS  premiums  denominated  in  U.S. 
2:34:1961:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:dollars and  a  foreign  currency—tell  us  how  financial  markets  view  the  interaction  between  a 
2:35:2064:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:country's likelihood of default and associated currency devaluations (the Twin Ds). A noarbitrage 
2:36:2161:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:model applied to the term structure of quanto spreads can isolate the interaction between the Twin 
2:37:2259:14:14:72:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:Ds  and  gauge  the  associated risk  premiums.  We  study  countries  in  the  Eurozone  because  their 
2:38:2363:14:14:72:543:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:quanto spreads pertain to the same exchange rate and monetary policy, allowing us to link cross-
2:39:2458:14:14:72:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:sectional variation in their term structures to cross-country differences in fiscal policies. The ratio 
2:40:2561:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:of the risk-adjusted to the true default intensities is 2, on average. Conditional on the occurrence 
2:41:2661:14:14:72:546:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:of  default,  the  true  and  risk-adjusted  1-week  probabilities of  devaluation  are  5%  and  77%, 
2:42:2763:14:14:71:546:462:12:Times:12:Times:C:respectively.  The  risk  premium  for  the  euro  devaluation  in  case  of default  exceeds  the  regular 
2:43:2870:14:28:72:280:448:12:Times:12:Times:C:currency premium by up to 0.3% per week.
2:44:2910:28:14:72:153:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:Patrick Augustin
2:45:2926:14:14:72:236:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:Desautels Faculty of Management
2:46:2957:14:14:72:160:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:McGill University
2:47:2974:14:14:72:269:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:1001 Sherbrooke Street West, Room 552
2:48:3011:14:14:72:231:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:Montreal, Qc  H3A 1G5  Canada
2:49:3040:14:28:72:204:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:patrick.augustin@mcgill.ca
2:50:3066:28:14:72:154:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:Mikhail Chernov
2:51:3081:14:14:72:234:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:Anderson School of Management
2:52:3110:14:14:72:254:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:University of California, Los Angeles
2:53:3147:14:14:72:237:280:12:Times:12:Times:C:110 Westwood Plaza, Suite C-417
2:54:3178:14:14:72:188:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:Los Angeles, CA 90095
2:55:3199:14:14:72:124:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:56:3207:14:0:72:248:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:mikhail.chernov@anderson.ucla.edu
2:57:3240:0:14:306:372:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:Dongho Song
2:58:3251:14:14:306:417:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:Carey Business School
2:59:3272:14:14:306:419:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:100 International Drive
2:60:3295:14:14:306:412:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:Baltimore, MD 21202
2:61:3314:14:0:306:414:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:dongho.song@jhu.edu
3:62:3333:0:36:90:203:691:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:1    Introduction
3:63:3350:36:14:90:522:655:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The risk of sovereign default and exchange rate fluctuations are inextricably linked.  The
3:64:3440:14:13:90:522:641:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:depreciation of a country’s currency is often a reflection of poor economic conditions.  De-
3:65:3532:13:14:90:522:628:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fault events tend to be associated with currency devaluations.  Such devaluations may either
3:66:3624:14:13:90:522:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:strategically support the competitiveness of the domestic economy, or penalize a country’s
3:67:3714:13:26:90:522:601:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:growth due to increased borrowing costs or reduced access to international capital markets.
3:68:3805:26:13:90:522:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Despite the importance of studying theTwin Ds(default and devaluation), the subject has
3:69:3892:13:14:90:522:562:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:received relatively limited attention in the literature.  In our view,  one reason for this is
3:70:3986:14:13:90:522:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that it is exceedingly difficult to measure the interaction between the two.  Indeed,  both
3:71:4077:13:14:90:522:535:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:types  of  events  are  rare,  so  few  data  are  available  for  researchers  to  use.   Disagreement
3:72:4180:14:13:90:521:521:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:over measurements are a clear manifestation of the problem.  For example,Reinhart(2002)
3:73:4267:13:14:89:521:508:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates the probability of devaluation conditional on default at 84%, whileNa, Schmitt-
3:74:4356:14:13:89:521:494:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Groh ́e,  Uribe,  and Yue(2017) find it to be 48%.  Another hard-to-measure dimension of
3:75:4444:13:14:89:521:481:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  Twin  Ds  is  whether  default  has  an  immediate  or  long-term  impact  on  the  exchange
3:76:4541:14:13:89:522:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rate.Krugman(1979) argues that default leads to a change in the expected depreciation
3:77:4626:13:14:89:522:454:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rate (change in exchange rate), whileNa, Schmitt-Groh ́e, Uribe, and Yue(2017) suggest a
3:78:4714:14:25:89:300:440:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:one-off drop in the exchange rate at default.
3:79:4759:25:14:89:521:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In this study, we are the first to take advantage of a recent development in financial markets
3:80:4853:14:13:89:521:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to offer an asset-pricing perspective on the measurement of the risk premia associated with
3:81:4944:13:14:89:521:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the Twin Ds.  Specifically, sovereign credit default swap (CDS) contracts are available in
3:82:5034:14:13:89:521:374:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:different currency denominations starting from August 2010.  For example, contracts that
3:83:5122:13:14:89:521:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:protect against a credit event in Germany could be denominated in euros (EUR) or U.S.
3:84:5207:14:13:89:521:347:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:dollars (USD) (we use the terms default and credit event interchangeably).  The difference
3:85:5297:13:14:89:522:334:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:between  the  two  respective  CDS  premiums  of  the  same  maturity,  also  known  asquanto
3:86:5390:14:13:89:522:320:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:CDS spread, reflects the market’s view about the interaction between the Twin Ds.  Quanto
3:87:5479:13:25:89:521:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spreads of different maturities are informative about the interaction over different horizons.
3:88:5573:25:14:89:521:282:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We focus on quanto spreads in the 17 European countries that share the euro as the common
3:89:5662:14:14:89:521:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:exchange rate.  We find the associated CDS markets particularly interesting for two reasons.
3:90:5754:14:13:89:521:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:First,  despite  the  common  currency  and  monetary  policy,  the  term  structures  of  quanto
3:91:5851:13:14:89:521:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spreads are different, suggesting intriguing implications regarding the different fiscal policies.
3:92:5949:14:13:89:521:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Second,  the  contractual  arrangements  of  the  European  contracts  make  observed  quanto
3:93:6042:13:14:89:521:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spreads transparent in terms of the implications for the Twin Ds.  Specifically, in contrast
3:94:6134:14:13:89:521:200:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to contracts for emerging markets (EM), payouts on Western European sovereign CDS of
3:95:6218:13:14:89:521:187:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:all denominations are triggered irrespective of whether a default is associated with domestic
3:96:6311:14:25:89:163:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:or foreign debt.
3:97:6327:25:13:89:521:148:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We start by explaining the institutional arrangements behind sovereign CDS in different
3:98:6414:13:14:89:521:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:currencies.  We then explain how quanto spreads are related to the interaction between the
3:99:6504:14:13:89:521:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Twin  Ds.   Next,  we  develop  a  model  that  allows  us  to  characterize  the  relation  between
3:100:6604:13:0:89:267:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:default and devaluation probabilities.
4:101:6643:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Describing  the  joint  behavior  of  17  different  term  structures  and  an  exchange  rate  is  a
4:102:6744:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:daunting task.  Therefore, we limit ourselves to a no-arbitrage affine term structure model
4:103:6835:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  allows  us  to  evaluate  whether  it  is  possible  to  reconcile  all  of  this  evidence  within
4:104:6940:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a tractable specification.  Along the way,  we encounter a typical problem in the analysis
4:105:7030:14:13:90:522:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of credit-sensitive financial instruments:  as the realization of credit events is rare, we can
4:106:7125:13:14:90:522:623:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:identify only the risk-adjusted distribution of these events based on asset prices.  We exploit
4:107:7220:14:13:90:522:609:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(i) the interaction between credit risk and currency risk, and (ii) the currency commonality
4:108:7312:13:14:90:522:596:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to identify the true distribution of credit events.  As a bonus,  our approach allows us to
4:109:7403:14:13:90:522:582:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:identify the loss given default (LGD), which we assume to be constant and the same for all
4:110:7493:13:14:90:522:569:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:countries.  While this assumption is an oversimplification, it nevertheless offers progress on
4:111:7587:14:24:90:223:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a thorny empirical problem.
4:112:7614:24:14:90:522:531:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  model  we  propose  features  the  following  critical  components:   a  model  of  the  U.S.
4:113:7712:14:14:90:522:517:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reference interest rate curve, a model of credit risk, and a model of the spot/forward FX
4:114:7801:14:13:90:522:503:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:curve.   We  use  overnight  indexed  swap  (OIS)  rates  as  a  reference  curve  and  construct  a
4:115:7901:13:25:90:290:490:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:two-factor model to capture its dynamics.
4:116:7942:25:13:90:522:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The starting point for our credit risk model is a credit event whose arrival is controlled by
4:117:8035:13:14:90:522:452:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a doubly-stochastic Cox process, a popular modeling device in the literature.  The default
4:118:8125:14:13:90:522:438:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:intensity  in  each  country  is  controlled  by  two  factors  –  global  and  regional  –  which  are
4:119:8228:13:14:90:522:425:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:weighted differently for each country.  We identify the global factor by setting the weights
4:120:8320:14:13:90:522:411:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on  Germany’s  regional  factors  to  zero.   Given  that  our  data  are  from  countries  in  the
4:121:8419:13:14:90:522:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Eurozone during the sovereign debt crisis, we derive an extension of our model to allow for
4:122:8510:14:13:90:522:384:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the possibility of credit contagion:  the occurrence of a credit event in one country affecting
4:123:8605:13:25:90:337:371:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the probability of a credit event in another country.
4:124:8658:25:13:90:522:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Last but not least, we model the behavior of the spot USD/EUR FX rate and the associated
4:125:8746:13:14:90:522:333:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:forward rates.  We follow the literature on realistic modeling of the time series on FX rates.
4:126:8840:14:14:90:522:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We allow for time-varying expected changes in the depreciation rate, heteroscedastic regular
4:127:8932:14:24:90:282:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:shocks to the rates, and extreme events.
4:128:8972:24:14:90:522:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We connect jumps in the FX rate to sovereign credit risk by requiring them to take place
4:129:9060:14:13:90:522:267:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:simultaneously with credit events.  This modeling feature is our identifying assumption that
4:130:9152:13:14:90:522:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:helps us to establish the true distribution of credit events.  To enhance the statistical relia-
4:131:9248:14:13:90:522:240:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bility of our estimates, we follow Bai, Collin-Dufresne, Goldstein, and Helwege(2015) and
4:132:9337:13:14:90:522:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:complement our identification strategy by associating realized credit events with extreme
4:133:9426:14:24:90:234:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:movements in quanto spreads.
4:134:9454:24:14:90:522:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  use  joint  data  on  the  term  structure  of  the  quanto  spreads  of  six  countries,  which
4:135:9554:14:13:90:522:175:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:represent  the  most  liquid  CDS  contracts  across  the  European  core  and  periphery,  some
4:136:9650:13:14:90:522:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:data on Greece prior to its credit event, the spot and forward FX rates, and a cross-section
4:137:9742:14:13:90:522:148:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  credit  events  for  the  six  countries.   We  estimate  the  model  via  the  Bayesian  Markov
4:138:9842:13:14:90:522:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) method.  The model offers an accurate fit to the data.  It also
4:139:9930:14:13:90:522:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fits the quanto spreads of the remaining 10 Eurozone countries that were not used in the
4:140:10018:13:0:90:143:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimation.
5:141:10030:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We find that a more parsimonious model without contagion fits the data just as well and
5:142:10117:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:does not differ significantly from the larger model in terms of its likelihood.  Therefore, we
5:143:10211:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:perform the rest of the analysis using the simpler model, which features only four factors:
5:144:10302:13:22:90:462:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:three credit factors (one global and two regional) and one FX variance factor.
5:145:10380:22:14:90:522:628:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We find a substantial cross-sectional variation in how the credit risks of countries load on
5:146:10472:14:13:90:522:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the credit factors.  For instance, exposure to the global factor varies from a high of 4 times
5:147:10566:13:14:90:522:601:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the German level (for Spain) to a low of 1/14 times (for Finland).  Finland is unambiguously
5:148:10658:14:13:90:522:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the least risky country.  There are multiple candidates,  primarily from Southern Europe,
5:149:10747:13:14:90:522:574:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for the most risky.  Some countries, both core and peripheral, have significant exposure to
5:150:10838:14:22:90:195:560:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the global factor only.
5:151:10861:22:14:90:522:538:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:As we conjectured earlier, a large part of this cross-sectional variation (44% to be precise)
5:152:10954:14:13:90:522:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is driven by differences in the fiscal policies as measured by a country’s debt.  A fixed effects
5:153:11051:13:14:90:522:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regression of hazard rates on the debt-to-GDP ratio implies that a one percentage point
5:154:11138:14:13:90:522:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:increase in the ratio of a given country is,  on average,  associated with an increase in its
5:155:11231:13:22:90:343:484:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CDS premium of approximately 8 basis points (bps).
5:156:11281:22:14:90:522:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our setting allows for the estimation of the true distribution of credit events.  As a result, we
5:157:11378:14:13:90:522:448:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:can characterize the time-varying credit risk premium, which is typically measured by the
5:158:11467:13:14:90:522:435:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ratio of the risk-adjusted to the true default intensity.  We find that the credit risk premium
5:159:11562:14:14:90:522:421:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is about 2, on average.  This estimate is consistent with earlier studies of corporate credit
5:160:11655:14:13:90:522:407:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk that were estimating a constant risk premium.  We also find evidence for a significant
5:161:11746:13:14:90:522:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:amount of variation over time, as the credit risk premium ranges between 1 and 6 during
5:162:11833:14:22:90:179:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our sample period.
5:163:11851:22:13:90:522:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our estimated model can also inform the measurement issues highlighted earlier.  For in-
5:164:11939:13:14:90:522:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:stance,  we  find  the  true  1-week  probability  of  devaluation  conditional  on  default  to  be
5:165:12039:14:13:90:522:331:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:4%, which is consistent with the view byNa, Schmitt-Groh ́e, Uribe, and Yue(2017) of a
5:166:12125:13:14:90:522:318:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:large drop in the exchange rate upon default.  In addition, we find that that the expected
5:167:12215:14:22:90:520:304:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:depreciation rate is unrelated to credit factors, contradicting the view ofKrugman(1979).
5:168:12304:22:14:90:522:282:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  risk-adjusted  probability  of  devaluation  conditional  on  default  is  75%,  suggesting  a
5:169:12403:14:13:90:522:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:hefty risk premium for this event.  Indeed, the model-implied risk premiums for exposure
5:170:12491:13:14:90:522:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to the Twin Ds exceed the regular currency risk premiums by as much as 0.3% per week.
5:171:12576:14:13:90:522:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Thus, the default-contingent currency risk premium is significantly larger than the default
5:172:12667:13:14:90:522:228:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk premium, which is suggestive of the large economic importance of that risk.  All of this
5:173:12760:14:13:90:522:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:evidence suggests that default-contingent devaluation, although not highly probable, occurs
5:174:12851:13:14:90:522:201:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:during the worst states of the economy when the marginal utility of investors is particularly
5:175:12944:14:37:90:114:187:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:high.
5:176:12949:37:29:90:195:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:Related literature
5:177:12967:29:13:90:522:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:This study is related to two strands of the literature.  First, it is most closely related to the
5:178:13064:13:0:90:521:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:literature on the relation between sovereign credit and currency risks.Della-Corte, Sarno,
6:179:13155:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Schmeling, and Wagner (2016) empirically show that the common component in sovereign
6:180:13239:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:credit risk correlates with currency depreciations and predicts currency risk premia.Carr
6:181:13328:14:13:90:521:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Wu(2007) propose a joint valuation framework for sovereign CDS and currency options
6:182:13415:13:14:90:521:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with  an  empirical  application  to  Mexico  and  Brazil.Du  and  Schreger(2016)  study  the
6:183:13508:14:13:90:522:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:determinants of local currency risk as a distinct component of foreign default risk in EM.
6:184:13598:13:14:90:522:623:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Buraschi, Sener, and Menguetuerk(2014) suggest that geographical funding frictions may
6:185:13684:14:13:90:522:609:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be responsible for persistent mispricing of EM bonds denominated in EUR and USD. While
6:186:13770:13:14:90:522:596:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:related, our work is conceptually different because of the aforementioned differences in the
6:187:13862:14:13:90:522:582:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:treatment of credit events associated with domestic and foreign debt.  We exploit the entire
6:188:13954:13:14:90:522:569:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:term structure of CDS quanto spreads to pin down the time variation in the risk premia
6:189:14040:14:25:90:481:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:associated with expectations of exchange rate depreciation conditional on default.
6:190:14122:25:14:90:522:530:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The most recent development in the joint FX-sovereign risk literature is research on CDS
6:191:14210:14:14:90:522:516:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quanto spreads.Mano(2013) proposes a descriptive segmented market model that is con-
6:192:14294:14:13:90:522:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sistent with nominal and real exchange rate depreciation upon an exogenous default trig-
6:193:14382:13:14:90:522:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ger.DeSantis(2015)  uses  quanto  spreads  to  construct  measures  of  redenomination  risk.
6:194:14475:14:13:90:522:475:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:No-arbitrage term structure models for quanto spreads are proposed byEhlers and Schoen-
6:195:14562:13:14:90:521:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bucher(2004)  for  Japanese  corporate  CDS,  and  byBrigo,  Pede,  and  Petrelli(2016)  for
6:196:14654:14:25:90:150:448:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Italian CDS.
6:197:14666:25:14:90:522:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In contemporaneous and independent work,Lando and Nielsen(2017);Monfort, Pegoraro,
6:198:14748:14:13:90:522:409:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Renne, and Roussellet(2017) develop models of sovereign quanto CDS spreads in the Eu-
6:199:14833:13:14:90:522:396:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rozone.  The former study is focused on the contribution of each of the normal and jump
6:200:14920:14:13:90:522:382:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risks to the shape of the quanto term structure.  The latter study uses quanto spreads in
6:201:15009:13:14:90:521:369:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a  modeling  application  of  the  Gamma-zero  distribution,  often  denoted  asARG0.   Both
6:202:15101:14:14:90:522:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:studies estimate their models of quanto spreads on a country-by-country basis, whereas we
6:203:15190:14:13:90:522:341:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:jointly model the exchange rate risk and quanto spreads for the entire term structure of six
6:204:15282:13:14:90:522:328:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:countries.  This distinction is important, because the dynamics of exchange rates in CDS
6:205:15370:14:13:90:522:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spreads ought to respect the common behavior of the EUR-USD exchange rate movements
6:206:15453:13:14:90:522:301:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in conjunction with the country-specific default risk.  In addition, using an identifying as-
6:207:15546:14:13:90:522:287:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sumption that exploits the common currency, we estimate both the true and risk-adjusted
6:208:15633:13:14:90:522:274:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:default intensities.  As a result, we can discuss the implications for time-varying risk premia
6:209:15728:14:13:90:522:260:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:associated with the default risk and the expected depreciation risk conditional on default.
6:210:15819:13:14:90:522:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Joint estimation is also necessary for identifying the propagation of shocks across countries,
6:211:15913:14:25:90:375:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that is, contagion, a subject of public and academic debate.
6:212:15973:25:14:90:522:208:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Second, our study builds on the vast literature on no-arbitrage affine term structure mod-
6:213:16063:14:14:90:522:194:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:eling  and  credit-sensitive  instruments,  prominently  summarized  inDuffie  and  Singleton
6:214:16156:14:13:90:522:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(2003).Duffie, Pedersen, and Singleton(2003),Hoerdahl and Tristani(2012), andMonfort
6:215:16240:13:14:90:522:167:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Renne(2013) study sovereign credit spreads.  With respect to the valuation of sovereign
6:216:16331:14:13:90:522:153:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CDS, the early affine term structure models focus on country-by-country estimations such
6:217:16419:13:14:90:521:140:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as Turkey, Brazil, Mexico (Pan and Singleton,2008), and Argentina (Zhang,2008), or on
6:218:16504:14:13:90:522:126:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a  panel  of  emerging  (Longstaff,  Pan,  Pedersen,  and  Singleton,2011),  or  developed  and
6:219:16599:13:0:90:521:113:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:emerging countries (Doshi,  Jacobs,  and Zurita,2017).Ang and Longstaff(2013) extract
7:220:16685:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a  common  systemic  factor  across  Europe  and  the  U.S.  using  sovereign  CDS  written  on
7:221:16780:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:European countries and U.S. states, while Ait-Sahalia, Laeven, and Pelizzon(2014) study
7:222:16867:14:25:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pairwise contagion among pairs of seven European countries during the sovereign debt crisis.
7:223:16959:25:14:90:522:638:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Most studies in this area do not estimate the LGD separately from the default intensity
7:224:17046:14:13:90:522:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:because of a joint identification problem.  Some papers are able to identify the LGD using
7:225:17136:13:14:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CDS  data  because  of  the  recovery  of  face  value  assumption  (Pan  and  Singleton,2008;
7:226:17230:14:13:90:522:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Elkamhi, Jacobs, and Pan,2014).Doshi, Elkamhi, and Ornthanalai(2017) exploit senior
7:227:17313:13:14:89:521:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  subordinate  CDS  to  identify  the  LGD.  Lastly,  the  most  recent  studies  exploit  the
7:228:17410:14:13:89:522:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:insensitivity of equity valuation to the LGD (Kuehn, Schreindorfer, and Schulz,2017;Li,
7:229:17497:13:14:89:521:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2017).  Our approach is more closely related to the first and the last studies because we
7:230:17586:14:25:89:515:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:assume recovery of face value and that a jump in exchange rate is unrelated to the LGD.
7:231:17673:25:14:89:521:518:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Finally,  we  use  a  model  of  contagion,  which  is  an  active  topic  in  the  recent  credit  risk
7:232:17777:14:13:89:522:504:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:literature.Bai, Collin-Dufresne, Goldstein, and Helwege(2015) emphasize that contagion
7:233:17863:13:14:89:521:491:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:should be an important component of credit risk pricing models in the context of a large
7:234:17951:14:13:89:522:477:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:number of corporate names.Benzoni, Collin-Dufresne, Goldstein, and Helwege(2015) offer
7:235:18037:13:14:89:521:464:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:evidence of contagion risk premiums in sovereign CDS spreads in the context of ambiguity-
7:236:18126:14:14:89:522:450:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:averse economic agents.Ait-Sahalia, Laeven, and Pelizzon(2014) find evidence of contagion
7:237:18215:14:13:89:521:436:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:under risk-adjusted probability in sovereign CDS spreads.Azizpour, Giesecke, and Schwen-
7:238:18303:13:14:89:522:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:kler(2018) find evidence of contagion in a descriptive model of realized corporate defaults.
7:239:18395:14:13:89:522:409:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Monfort, Pegoraro, Renne, and Roussellet(2017) reach a similar conclusion in the context
7:240:18483:13:26:89:502:396:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of bank CDS. We study contagion under both the risk-adjusted and true probabilities.
7:241:18567:26:13:89:522:370:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:A table in AppendixF summarizes the specific modeling elements across the key studies with
7:242:18657:13:14:89:521:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:affine intensity-based frameworks for sovereign credit spreads.  The table visually highlights
7:243:18751:14:13:89:521:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the primary differences between the current study and others.  Methodologically, our work
7:244:18840:13:47:89:306:330:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:encompasses most of the existing approaches.
7:245:18884:47:36:89:396:283:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:2    Sovereign CDS contracts and currencies
7:246:18927:36:33:89:274:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:2.1    Cash flows and settlement
7:247:18959:33:13:89:521:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Sovereign CDS are contracts that pay off in case of a sovereign credit event.  This section
7:248:19050:13:14:89:521:201:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reviews what such an event represents.  Given the focus on USD/EUR quantos of Eurozone
7:249:19136:14:13:89:521:187:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:countries, we limit the discussion to the legal details associated with European contracts.
7:250:19227:13:26:89:170:174:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:See AppendixA.
7:251:19241:26:13:89:521:148:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We useStto denote the nominal USD/EUR FX rate (amount of USD per EUR) at timet.
7:252:19320:13:14:89:521:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The first row of Figure1 depicts the cash flows associated with a EUR-denominated CDS
7:253:19405:14:13:89:521:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:contract (long protection) with a premium ofeCe0established at time 0 (the time of the
7:254:19491:13:0:89:521:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:contract’s maturityTis omitted for brevity).  In this example, the notional is $1 =e(1/S0),
8:255:19583:0:14:90:521:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:implying an annualized payment ofeCe0/S0.For the purpose of this discussion, we ignore
8:256:19669:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the quarterly or semi-annual frequency of the premium payment settlement, and focus on the
8:257:19759:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:annual amounts.  The second row shows a USD-denominated contract (short protection)
8:258:19842:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with  a  premium  of  $C$0.Given  the  same  notional,  the  annual  payment  is  $C$0,which  is
8:259:19938:14:24:90:440:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:equivalent toeC$0/Stat the spot exchange rates on the settlement dates.
8:260:20009:24:14:90:522:612:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We highlight three implications of the rules that are particularly relevant for this paper.
8:261:20100:14:13:90:522:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:First, a credit event that affects all CDS contracts regardless of the currency of denomination
8:262:20195:13:14:90:522:585:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:could be triggered by a default pertaining to a subset of bonds, such as a sovereign defaulting
8:263:20290:14:13:90:522:571:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on domestic debt but not on bonds issued in other jurisdictions.  Therefore, a CDS quanto
8:264:20379:13:14:90:522:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spread would not reflect the risk of selective default. This is in contrast to EM bonds, studied
8:265:20475:14:13:90:522:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by Du and Schreger (2016), where differences between the credit spreads denominated in
8:266:20561:13:14:90:522:531:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:USD and local currency could reflect such a risk,  and to EM CDS contracts,  studied by
8:267:20648:14:14:90:522:517:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Mano (2013), for which a credit event is not triggered by default on domestic currency or
8:268:20737:14:24:90:186:503:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:domestic law bonds.
8:269:20756:24:14:90:522:479:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Second,  an obligation is deemed deliverable into the contract settlement regardless of its
8:270:20847:14:13:90:522:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:currency of denomination or that of the CDS contract.  This means that one and the same
8:271:20934:13:14:90:522:452:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bond could be delivered into the settlements of CDS contracts of different denominations.
8:272:21023:14:13:90:521:438:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Thus, recovery is free of any exchange rate consideration, a point also made byEhlers and
8:273:21112:13:14:90:521:425:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Schoenbucher(2004).  Compare this withMano(2013), who, in the context of EM bonds
8:274:21193:14:24:89:457:411:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:explicitly considers different currency denominations of the recovery amount.
8:275:21270:24:14:89:521:387:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:As an extreme example, imagine a European sovereign that has 1% of all its debt issued
8:276:21356:14:13:89:521:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in EUR, and the rest issued in USD. Both EUR- and USD-denominated contracts would
8:277:21437:13:14:89:521:360:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be  triggered  in  the  case  of  selective  default  on  the  small  amount  of  outstanding  EUR-
8:278:21536:14:13:89:521:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:denominated debt.  Because one can deliver a bond of any denomination into a contract
8:279:21621:13:14:89:521:333:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of any denomination, the cash value of payments in case of a credit event could be viewed
8:280:21710:14:14:89:521:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as an identical fraction, denoted byL(LGD) in Figure1, of a contract’s notional amount.
8:281:21797:14:13:89:522:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We fixLto be a constant, in line with the literature on CDS pricing (Pan and Singleton,
8:282:21884:13:25:89:481:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2008).  This removes any uncertainty about payments in the respective currencies.
8:283:21965:25:13:89:521:267:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The only uncertainty that arises with a credit event is due to expressing these payments
8:284:22053:13:14:89:521:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the same currency.  For example, the EUR-denominated contract pays a certain amount
8:285:22139:14:13:89:521:240:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:ofL/S0, while the EUR value of the payment of the USD-denominated contract isL/Sτ,
8:286:22221:13:14:89:521:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:withτdenoting  the  time  of  a  credit  event.   This  comparison  illustrates  the  impact  of
8:287:22317:14:13:89:522:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:devaluation.  If the EUR devalues during the credit event,Sτis lower thanS0, and, as a
8:288:22403:13:14:89:521:200:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:result, the value of the payment on the EUR-denominated contract is lower than that on
8:289:22489:14:24:89:218:186:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the USD-denominated one.
8:290:22513:24:14:89:521:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Third,  outright  default  is  only  one  of  the  scenarios  that  may  trigger  a  credit  event.   A
8:291:22616:14:13:89:521:148:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:common  concern  among  observers  of  the  Eurozone  credit  market  is  that  a  CDS  payout
8:292:22710:13:14:89:521:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:would be triggered by a restructuring of a Eurozone member country’s liabilities through a
8:293:22800:14:13:89:521:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:redenomination of the principal or interest payments into the country’s pre-EUR currency.
8:294:22889:13:0:89:521:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:There are two CDS definitions, those of 2003 and 2014, which treat this event differently.
9:295:22980:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:For contracts based on the 2003 definitions, redenomination does not trigger a credit event
9:296:23071:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as long as it involves the currencies of the G7 countries and AAA-rated OECD economies.
9:297:23158:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  newer  definitions  limit  these  currencies  to  the  lawful  currencies  of  Canada,  Japan,
9:298:23257:13:26:90:492:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Switzerland, the United Kingdom, the United States of America, and the Eurozone.
9:299:23337:26:13:90:522:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:After  the  2014  definitions  were  introduced,  CDS  could  be  concurrently  traded  satisfying
9:300:23435:13:14:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:either definition.  We use data on the contracts guided by the 2003 definitions throughout
9:301:23525:14:13:90:522:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our full sample to ensure internal consistency.Kremens(2018) explores the differences in
9:302:23613:13:14:90:522:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:premiums for the two types of contracts.  Regardless of the definition used, some countries
9:303:23704:14:13:90:522:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:might trigger a credit event by redenomination.  Our framework automatically accounts for
9:304:23793:13:14:90:522:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  because  our  credit  factors  are  designed  to  capture  the  probability  of  a  credit  event
9:305:23896:14:41:90:221:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:without discerning its type.
9:306:23924:41:33:90:285:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:2.2    Relation to sovereign bonds
9:307:23958:33:13:90:522:469:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Historically,  Eurozone  sovereign  CDS  were  denominated  in  USD  only.   One  point  worth
9:308:24052:13:14:90:522:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:emphasizing is that EUR-denominated CDS contracts that were introduced in 2010 are not
9:309:24138:14:13:90:522:442:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:redundant securities.  One might think of cash flows as similar to those of a portfolio that
9:310:24230:13:14:90:521:429:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:consists of a USD-denominated bond and a currency swap (e.g.,Du and Schreger,2016).
9:311:24313:14:13:90:522:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:However, such a strategy does not hedge the behavior of the FX rate conditional on default
9:312:24403:13:26:90:284:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:– the risk that is the focus of this paper.
9:313:24446:26:13:90:521:376:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To  see  this,  consider  the  third  and  fourth  rows  of  Figure1,  which  show  cash  flows  to  a
9:314:24548:13:14:90:522:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sovereign par bond and a currency swap of matching maturity.  The bond is USD denomi-
9:315:24633:14:14:90:522:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:nated, but the issuer prefers a EUR exposure, hence the additional swap position.  The cash
9:316:24724:14:25:90:328:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:flows are presented per $1 of face/notional values.
9:317:24775:25:14:90:522:310:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:At time 0, the issuer sells the bond for $1 and swaps this amount for the equivalent value
9:318:24865:14:13:90:521:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in EUR,e1/S0.Prior to maturity, the issuer has to pay interest of $C0on a bond, which
9:319:24950:13:14:90:522:283:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:it receives from the swap as interest on the USD value of the notional.  In exchange, the
9:320:25039:14:13:90:521:269:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:issuer has to pay interest ofeF0/S0on the EUR value of the swap, withF0denoting the
9:321:25122:13:26:90:322:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:currency swap rate that is determined at time 0.
9:322:25170:26:13:90:522:230:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:If there is no credit event, the last transaction takes place at maturity, where the issuer has
9:323:25265:13:14:90:522:217:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to repay $(1 +C0) on the bond and the EUR/USD notionals combined with the last interest
9:324:25352:14:13:90:522:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:payments that are exchanged in the swap transaction.  As a result, the combined position
9:325:25440:13:14:90:521:190:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f7:B:has a pure EUR exposure with pre-determined cash flows:e1/S0at inception,−eF0/S0
9:326:25520:14:13:89:522:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:thereafter (including the day of maturity), and−e1/S0at maturity.  This is conceptually
9:327:25607:13:14:89:521:163:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:similar to cash flows on the EUR-denominated sovereign CDS if there is no credit event
9:328:25693:14:26:89:385:149:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(the difference is in the latter being an unfunded instrument).
9:329:25756:26:13:89:521:123:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:If there is a credit event, then the bond-swap combination faces uncertain cash flows between
9:330:25849:13:0:89:521:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the time of the eventτand maturityT.The bond pays $(1−L) atτand ceases to exist.  In
10:331:25934:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the meantime, the swap does not terminate (assuming no counterparty risk) and continues
10:332:26021:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  exchange  of  cash  flows.   As  a  result,  the  values  of  the  combined  cash  flows  in  EUR
10:333:26123:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are  (L+C0−1)/Sτ−F0/S0atτ,  andC0/St−F0/S0forτ < t≤T.In  contrast,  the
10:334:26194:13:41:90:408:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:EUR-denominated sovereign CDS has a single cash flow ofeL/S0.
10:335:26255:41:33:90:362:609:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:2.3    Interpretation of the quanto CDS spread
10:336:26301:33:13:90:522:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure 1 allows us to take a first step toward thinking about quanto CDS spreads.  Adding
10:337:26390:13:14:90:522:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:up the two positions described in the first two rows (long EUR-denominated and short USD-
10:338:26479:14:13:90:522:549:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:denominated protection) gives an exposure to devaluation conditional on default, because
10:339:26567:13:14:90:522:536:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  only  uncertain  cash  flow  is  the  EUR  value  ofLin  the  USD  contract.   Specifically,
10:340:26664:14:14:90:522:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by  buying  the  EUR-denominated  protection  and  selling  the  USD-denominated  one,  we
10:341:26754:14:13:90:522:508:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:construct  a  position  that  benefits  if  there  is  no  EUR  devaluation  conditional  on  default.
10:342:26856:13:26:90:331:495:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:The payouteL(S−10−S−1τ) is negative ifSτ< S0.
10:343:26901:26:13:90:522:469:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Because CDS contracts have a fixed time to maturity, we observe premiums for new con-
10:344:26986:13:14:90:522:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tracts  in  every  period.   In  other  words,  we  only  get  to  see  the  difference  between  the
10:345:27087:14:13:90:521:442:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:premiumse(C$0−Ce0)/S0.Because the choice of notional is arbitrary, the quanto spread
10:346:27171:13:26:90:423:429:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:C$0−Ce0becomes the relevant premium for exposure to the Twin Ds.
10:347:27235:26:13:90:522:403:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To  streamline  the  analytical  interpretation  of  the  quanto  CDS  spread,  consider  a  hypo-
10:348:27333:13:14:90:522:390:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:thetical contract that trades all points upfront, meaning that a protection buyer pays the
10:349:27423:14:13:90:521:376:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:entire premium at timet.Further,  assume that the risk-free rate is constant.  Then,  the
10:350:27512:13:25:90:311:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:EUR-denominated CDS premium simplifies to
10:351:27553:25:24:130:481:338:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:C:Ce0=L·E0[M0,τI(τ≤T)Sτ∧T/S0]≡L·E∗0[e−r(τ∧T)I(τ≤T)Sτ∧T/S0],
10:352:27610:24:14:90:521:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whereMdenotes the USD-denominated pricing kernel,∗refers to the risk-adjusted prob-
10:353:27693:14:14:90:521:300:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ability, andI(·) is an indicator variable.  The USD-denominated premium is similar.  As a
10:354:27782:14:24:90:259:286:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:result, the relative quanto spread is
10:355:27819:24:16:143:181:262:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:C:C$0−Ce0
10:356:27826:16:0:157:169:246:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:C:C$0
10:357:27829:0:0:196:204:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:=
10:358:27830:0:15:215:388:262:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:A:E∗0[e−r(τ∧T)I(τ≤T) (1−Sτ∧T/S0)]
10:359:27861:15:27:250:353:247:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:A:E∗0[e−r(τ∧T)I(τ≤T)]
10:360:27880:27:0:196:226:220:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f7:A:=E∗0
10:361:27884:0:15:229:235:235:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:[
10:362:27885:15:0:235:251:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f10:A:1−
10:363:27887:0:15:255:277:227:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:C:Sτ∧T
10:364:27891:15:0:261:272:212:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:C:S0
10:365:27893:0:15:280:286:235:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:]
10:366:27894:15:0:288:318:220:11:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f7:C:−cov∗0
10:367:27900:0:11:321:327:238:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:[
10:368:27901:11:15:336:419:227:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:A:e−r(τ∧T)I(τ≤T)
10:369:27915:15:0:329:426:212:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:A:E∗0e−r(τ∧T)I(τ≤T)
10:370:27932:0:0:427:430:220:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:C:,
10:371:27933:0:15:433:455:227:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:C:Sτ∧T
10:372:27937:15:0:439:450:212:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:C:S0
10:373:27939:0:18:458:464:238:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:]
10:374:27940:18:34:466:522:220:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:A:,(1)
10:375:27944:34:13:90:522:186:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:where∧denotes the smallest of the two variables.  The first term reflects the risk-adjusted
10:376:28035:13:14:90:522:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expected currency depreciation, conditional on a credit event (a positive number corresponds
10:377:28127:14:0:90:522:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to EUR devaluation).  The covariance term reflects the interaction of default and FX risks.
11:378:28219:0:33:90:149:691:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:2.4    Data
11:379:28230:33:33:90:116:658:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:CDS
11:380:28233:33:13:90:522:625:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Sovereign CDS contracts became widely available in multiple currencies in 2010.  This de-
11:381:28322:13:14:90:522:612:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:termines the beginning of our sample, which runs from August 20, 2010 to December 30,
11:382:28407:14:13:90:522:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2016.  We source daily CDS premiums denominated in USD and EUR from Markit for all
11:383:28489:13:14:90:522:585:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:19 Eurozone countries.  We require a minimum of 365 days of non-missing information on
11:384:28575:14:13:90:522:571:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:USD/EUR quanto spreads.  This requirement excludes Malta and Luxembourg.  Thus, our
11:385:28658:13:14:90:522:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sample  features  17  countries:  Austria,  Belgium,  Cyprus,  Estonia,  Finland,  France,  Ger-
11:386:28754:14:13:90:522:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:many, Greece, Ireland, Italy, Latvia, Lithuania, Netherlands, Portugal, Slovakia, Slovenia,
11:387:28845:13:26:90:141:531:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Spain.
11:388:28855:26:13:90:522:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We work with weekly data to minimize noise due to the potential staleness of some of the
11:389:28943:13:14:90:522:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:prices and to maximize the continuity in subsequently observed prices.  We have continuous
11:390:29033:14:14:90:522:478:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:information on 5-year quanto spreads throughout the sample period for all countries except
11:391:29123:14:13:90:522:464:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Greece,  as  the  trading  of  its  sovereign  CDS  contract  halted  following  its  official  default
11:392:29226:13:14:90:522:451:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  2012.   In  addition,  we  retain  the  maturities  of  1,  3,  7,  10,  and  15  years  (we  omit  the
11:393:29333:14:13:90:522:437:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:available 30-year contracts because they are similar to the 15-year ones; in particular the
11:394:29424:13:14:90:522:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:term structures between 15 and 30 are flat).  Although the 5-year contract is the most liquid,
11:395:29518:14:13:90:522:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:liquidity across the term structure is less of a concern for sovereign CDS spreads than for
11:396:29609:13:14:90:522:397:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:corporate CDS spreads, as trading is more evenly spread across the maturity spectrum (Pan
11:397:29698:14:25:90:191:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Singleton, 2008).
11:398:29719:25:14:90:522:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Although these sovereign CDS contracts trade in multiple currencies, there might be differ-
11:399:29810:14:13:90:522:344:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ences in liquidity given that an insurance payment in EUR would probably be less valuable
11:400:29899:13:14:90:522:331:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:if Germany defaulted.  Consistent with this view, USD-denominated contracts tend to be
11:401:29985:14:14:90:522:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:more liquid, as documented in Table1, which reports the average number of dealers quoting
11:402:30074:14:13:90:521:303:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:such contracts in either EUR or USD over time; that is, CDS depth (Qiu and Yu,2012).
11:403:30158:13:14:90:522:290:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The average difference between the number of USD and EUR dealers ranges between 0.60
11:404:30242:14:13:90:522:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  2.66.   EUR  CDS  contracts  are  quoted  by  2.73  to  6.30  dealers,  on  average,  which  is
11:405:30342:13:14:90:522:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:economically meaningful given that the CDS market is largely concentrated among a hand-
11:406:30429:14:13:90:521:249:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ful of dealers (Giglio,2014;Siriwardane,2014).  In relative terms, the average number of
11:407:30517:13:14:90:522:236:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quoting dealers for the USD contracts exceeds that for the EUR by 1.  That suggests that
11:408:30605:14:25:90:410:222:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the difference in liquidity of the two types of contracts is not large.
11:409:30676:25:14:90:521:197:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Notional amounts outstanding, also reported in Table1, offer a sense of the cross-sectional
11:410:30767:14:13:90:522:183:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variation in the size of the market. Regardless of the currency of denomination, the notionals
11:411:30861:13:14:90:522:170:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are converted into USD and reported on the gross and net basis.  To facilitate comparison,
11:412:30951:14:14:90:522:156:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we express these numbers as a percentage of the respective quantities for Italy, which has the
11:413:31045:14:13:90:521:142:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:largest gross and net notionals (Augustin, Sokolovski, Subrahmanyam, and Tomio,2016).
11:414:31130:13:14:90:522:129:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The amounts for France, Germany, and Spain stand out as a fraction of Italy’s amounts,
11:415:31216:14:0:90:301:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:followed by Austria, Belgium, and Portugal.
12:416:31260:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To provide a first feel for the data, Figure 2A displays the time-series of one of the most liquid
12:417:31358:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  arguably  the  least  credit-risky  CDS  contracts,  namely  the  5-year  USD-denominated
12:418:31452:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:contract for Germany.  We highlight important events to help frame the magnitudes of CDS
12:419:31540:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:premiums.  The premium for such a safe country is about 20 bps during the calmest periods,
12:420:31630:14:25:90:400:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:varies over time, and exceeds 100 bps during the sovereign crisis.
12:421:31696:25:14:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To  further  gauge  the  size  of  the  market  for  single-name  sovereign  CDS,  we  compare  the
12:422:31795:14:13:90:522:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:gross notional amounts outstanding to the aggregate market size.Augustin(2014) reports
12:423:31881:13:14:90:522:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that in 2012,  single-name sovereign CDS accounted for approximately 11% of the overall
12:424:31968:14:13:90:522:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:market, which was then valued at $27 trillion in gross notional amounts outstanding.  The
12:425:32057:13:14:90:522:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:corporate CDS market accounted for about 89% of the market, with single- and multi-name
12:426:32144:14:13:90:522:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:contracts amounting to $16 trillion and $11 trillion, respectively.  While the CDS market
12:427:32233:13:14:90:522:530:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:has somewhat shrunk in recent years, statistics from the Bank for International Settlements
12:428:32324:14:14:90:522:516:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:suggest that sovereign CDS represented $1.715 trillion, about 18% of the entire market, in
12:429:32414:14:40:90:115:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2016.
12:430:32419:40:33:90:175:462:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Quanto spreads
12:431:32433:33:13:90:521:429:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Table2  provides  basic  summary  statistics  for  the  quanto  spreads.   There  is  a  significant
12:432:32533:13:14:90:522:416:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:amount of both cross-sectional and time-series variation in the spreads.  In the cross-section,
12:433:32628:14:14:90:522:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the average quanto spread ranges from 6 bps for Estonia to 90 bps for Greece, at the 5-year
12:434:32719:14:13:90:522:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:maturity.   The  average  quanto  slope,  defined  as  the  difference  between  the  10-year  and
12:435:32817:13:14:90:522:375:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:1-year quanto spreads, ranges from -29 bps for Greece to 29 bps for France.  Overall, both
12:436:32907:14:25:90:505:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the level and slope of CDS quanto spreads vary significantly over time in each country.
12:437:32994:25:14:90:522:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We limit the estimation of our model to data on six sovereigns because of parameter prolif-
12:438:33085:14:13:90:522:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:eration.  We choose the countries that exhibit the greatest market liquidity and the fewest
12:439:33176:13:14:90:522:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:missing observations.  In addition, we incorporate both peripheral and core countries that
12:440:33266:14:13:90:522:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:feature the greatest variation in the average term structure of CDS quanto spreads.  This
12:441:33355:13:14:90:521:282:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:leads us to focus on Germany, Belgium, France, Ireland, Italy, and Spain.  Figure3A plots
12:442:33444:14:13:90:522:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the average quanto term spreads of different maturities for these countries.  We also use a
12:443:33535:13:14:90:522:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:limited amount of data on Greece, as described later in this section.  We use data on the
12:444:33624:14:41:90:452:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:remaining countries to conduct an “out-of-sample” evaluation of our model.
12:445:33698:41:32:90:168:200:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Exchange rate
12:446:33711:32:14:90:522:168:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  collect  the  time  series  of  the  USD/EUR  FX  rate  from  the  Federal  Reserve  Bank  of
12:447:33808:14:13:90:522:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:St.  Louis Economic Database (FRED) and match it with the quanto data, using weekly
12:448:33891:13:14:90:522:141:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:exchange rates, sampled every Wednesday.  Figures2B and3B display the exchange rate
12:449:33974:14:13:90:522:127:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  (log)  depreciation  rate,  respectively.   A  broad  devaluation  of  the  EUR  is  evident  in
12:450:34075:13:0:90:140:114:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure2B.
13:451:34086:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure  3B  suggests  that  the  exchange  rate  movements  were  close  to  being  independent
13:452:34181:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and identically distributed (iid) during our sample period.  Motivated by that, Appendix
13:453:34269:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:B shows that the term structure of credit premia is flat if both the default intensity and
13:454:34359:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:depreciation rates are iid but correlated with each other.  This result establishes a useful
13:455:34451:14:25:90:410:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:benchmark for interpreting the evidence summarized in Figure 3A.
13:456:34515:25:14:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CDS premiums and exchange rates are interrelated and move together over time.  This is
13:457:34601:14:13:90:522:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:summarized by the cross-correlogram between the first principal component of changes in
13:458:34688:13:14:90:522:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:5-year CDS premiums and depreciation rates in Figure 2C. The Figure highlights that this
13:459:34776:14:25:90:486:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interaction is primarily contemporaneous, and not readily visible in leads and lags.
13:460:34860:25:14:90:522:545:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure 2D stays with Germany to show an example of time-series variation in (5-year) quanto
13:461:34951:14:13:90:521:531:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CDS spreads.  As explained in Section2.3, the spreads reflect the interaction between the
13:462:35040:13:14:90:522:518:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Twin Ds and are informative about the covariance risk and the currency jump at default
13:463:35126:14:14:90:522:504:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk.  A model is needed to understand the interactions over different horizons and to extract
13:464:35220:14:40:90:212:490:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the quanto risk premium.
13:465:35244:40:33:90:164:450:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Interest rates
13:466:35258:33:13:90:522:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To develop the model, we also need information on the term structure of U.S. interest rates.
13:467:35350:13:14:90:522:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Prior to the global financial crisis (GFC) of 2008/09, it was common practice to use Libor
13:468:35440:14:13:90:522:390:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  swap  rates  as  the  closest  approximation  to  risk-free  lending  rates  in  the  interdealer
13:469:35542:13:14:90:521:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:market (Feldhutter and Lando,2008).  Since the GFC, practitioners have shifted toward
13:470:35627:14:14:90:522:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:full collateralization and started using OIS rates as better proxies of risk-free rates (Hull and
13:471:35724:14:13:90:522:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:White,2013).  This shift has implications for Libor-linked interest rate swaps (IRS) because
13:472:35816:13:14:90:522:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:discounting  is  performed  using  the  OIS-implied  curves.   We  source  daily  information  on
13:473:35913:14:13:90:522:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:OIS and IRS rates for all available maturities from Bloomberg, focusing on OIS rates with
13:474:36002:13:14:90:522:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:maturities of 3, 6, 9, 12, 36, and 60 months and IRS rates with maturities of 7, 10, 15, and
13:475:36094:14:25:90:132:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:30 years.
13:476:36103:25:14:90:522:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  bootstrap  zero  coupon  rates  from  all  swap  rates.   We  transform  all  swap  rates  into
13:477:36202:14:13:90:522:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:par-bond yields, assuming a piece-wise constant forward curve, and then extract the zero-
13:478:36291:13:14:90:522:243:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:coupon rates of the same maturities as the swap rates.  Thus, we obtain a zero-coupon yield
13:479:36382:14:13:90:522:229:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimated from OIS rates up to 5 years, and from IRS rates for maturities above 5 years.
13:480:36470:13:14:90:522:216:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To extend the OIS zero-curve for maturities beyond 5 years, we use the zero-coupon yield
13:481:36558:14:14:90:522:202:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bootstrapped from IRS rates, but adjusted daily by the differential between the IRS- and
13:482:36646:14:25:90:497:188:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:OIS-implied zero-coupon curves.  A figure in AppendixGdisplays the resulting rates.
13:483:36729:25:14:90:522:163:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Once  we  have  a  model  of  the  joint  behavior  of  interest  rates  and  exchange  rates,  it  has
13:484:36832:14:13:90:522:149:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:implications for forward exchange rates.  To discipline our model, we use weekly Thomson
13:485:36920:13:14:90:522:136:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Reuters data on forward exchange rates obtained from Datastream.  We use the Wednesday
13:486:37006:14:13:90:522:122:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quotes for our analysis to match the Wednesday OIS rates and quanto spreads focusing on
13:487:37093:13:0:90:522:109:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the maturities of 1 week and 1 month.  Our analysis does not require the European interest
14:488:37185:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rate values, hence we can avoid addressing the important analysis of CIP violations in Du,
14:489:37275:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Tepper,  and  Verdelhan(2017).   Covered  interest  parity  holds  in  our  model.   Therefore,
14:490:37370:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the inferred foreign interest rate could be viewed as an implicit foreign bank funding rate.
14:491:37462:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Such an interpretation is valid in the light of research focusing on various market frictions
14:492:37555:14:13:90:521:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:leading to violations of CIP in terms of true Libor rates (e.g.,Borio, McCauley, McGuire,
14:493:37644:13:41:90:180:623:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Sushko,2016).
14:494:37661:41:33:90:164:582:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Credit events
14:495:37674:33:13:90:522:549:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our last piece of evidence pertains to the true occurrence of credit events.  True default
14:496:37764:13:14:90:522:536:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:information is insufficient for estimating conditional credit event probabilities because re-
14:497:37857:14:13:90:522:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:alized  credit  events  are  rare.   This  issue  is  common  to  the  literature  on  credit-sensitive
14:498:37960:13:14:90:522:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:instruments.   When  modeling  corporate  defaults,  it  is  possible  to  infer  something  about
14:499:38058:14:13:90:522:495:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:true conditional default probabilities by grouping companies by their credit rating, as done
14:500:38150:13:26:90:244:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:byDriessen(2005), for instance.
14:501:38181:26:13:90:522:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We are considering high quality sovereign names, so we have only the credit event in Greece
14:502:38272:13:14:90:522:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  our  sample.   Formal  defaults  are  often  avoided  because  of  bailouts,  as  was  witnessed
14:503:38372:14:13:90:522:429:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:multiple times during the sovereign debt crisis (Greece, Ireland, Portugal, Spain, Cyprus).
14:504:38463:13:14:90:522:416:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:These bailouts result in large movements in credit spreads, although no formal credit event
14:505:38554:14:14:90:522:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:occurred.  Therefore, we associate credit events with extreme movements in quanto spreads
14:506:38643:14:13:90:522:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(see alsoBai, Collin-Dufresne, Goldstein, and Helwege,2015).  Specifically, we deem a credit
14:507:38735:13:14:90:522:375:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:event to have occurred if a weekly (Wednesday to Wednesday) change in the 5-year quanto
14:508:38822:14:13:90:522:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spread  is  above  the  99th  percentile  of  the  country-specific  distribution  of  quanto  spread
14:509:38923:13:14:90:522:348:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:changes.1A figure in AppendixG displays the observed credit events identified in this way
14:510:39012:14:25:90:254:334:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for the 16 countries in our sample.
14:511:39047:25:14:90:522:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Although Greece experienced a formal credit event, it is difficult to use the full available
14:512:39139:14:13:90:522:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:series for pragmatic reasons (see alsoAit-Sahalia, Laeven, and Pelizzon,2014).  As a figure
14:513:39230:13:14:90:522:282:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  AppendixGshows,  the  Greek  CDS  premium  jumped  to  5,062  bps  on  September  13,
14:514:39319:14:13:90:522:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2011, long before the true declaration of the credit event on March 9, 2012.  It exceeded the
14:515:39412:13:14:90:522:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:10,000 bps threshold, which is equivalent to 100% of the insured face value, on February 15,
14:516:39504:14:14:90:522:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2012.  Furthermore, trading of Greece CDS spreads was halted between March 8, 2012 and
14:517:39590:14:13:90:522:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:June 10, 2013, so the time series exhibits a long gap in quoted premiums.  Assuming the
14:518:39677:13:14:90:522:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Markit-reported aggregation of quoted spreads was tradable, Greek CDS trading restarted
14:519:39764:14:13:90:522:200:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on June 10, 2013, at a level of 978 bps.  The corresponding quanto spreads displayed in the
14:520:39855:13:14:90:522:187:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:same figure exhibit similar swings in magnitudes and gaps in the data.  These data problems
14:521:39946:14:13:90:522:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:create severe credit risk identification issues and make it difficult to study the joint behavior
14:522:40043:13:14:90:247:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of credit factors across countries.
14:523:40078:14:15:102:521:146:6:g_d0_f14:9:g_d0_f15:F:1One concern is that such a definition may bias downwards the coincidence of large drops in the EUR
14:524:40177:15:11:90:522:131:9:g_d0_f15:9:g_d0_f15:F:value and credit events.  Changing from quanto spreads to USD CDS premiums or introducing an identicial
14:525:40280:11:11:90:522:120:9:g_d0_f15:9:g_d0_f15:F:cut-off (two standard deviations of all CDS premiums changes across time and countries) does not materially
14:526:40387:11:0:90:399:109:9:g_d0_f15:9:g_d0_f15:F:affect estimated probabilities of the coincidence of these two types of events.
15:527:40468:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:As a result, we designate September 7, 2011, as a credit event instead of the official one.
15:528:40559:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:After  that  day,  the  available  data  are  unusable.   This  period  is  too  short  to  identify  the
15:529:40664:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Greek default hazard rate throughout the full sample.  Therefore,  we also use some data
15:530:40752:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from the period when the trading resumed in June 2013.  Out of concern that very large
15:531:40838:14:13:90:522:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:premiums  may  not  be  reflective  of  true  traded  prices,  we  use  only  those  premiums  that
15:532:40937:13:14:90:522:623:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are within 150% of the maximum of premiums with a corresponding maturity among the
15:533:41019:14:13:90:522:609:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:remaining GIIPS countries.  The omitted premiums are so large, that the estimation results
15:534:41109:13:46:90:377:596:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are not sensitive to the choice of the maximum cutoff point.
15:535:41169:46:36:90:190:550:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:3    The model
15:536:41183:36:13:90:522:514:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In this section, we present a no-arbitrage model of the joint dynamics of U.S. interest rates,
15:537:41277:13:14:90:522:501:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:USD/EUR FX rate, forward FX rates, and CDS quanto spreads for Eurozone countries.  In
15:538:41362:14:14:90:522:487:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:broad strokes, the key part of the model is the connection between a devaluation of the FX
15:539:41452:14:13:90:522:473:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rate and a sovereign credit event.  Mathematically, we model the arrival of a credit event
15:540:41542:13:14:90:522:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:via a Poisson process.  Credit hazard rates feature one common component that is linked
15:541:41629:14:13:90:522:446:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to Germany, and regional components.  Furthermore, we allow for default contagion effects.
15:542:41719:13:14:90:522:433:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To connect devaluation to credit risk, we make the identifying assumption that jumps in
15:543:41806:14:13:90:522:419:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the FX rate can take place only if one of the Eurozone sovereigns experiences a credit event.
15:544:41899:13:14:90:521:406:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:This assumption is motivated by Figure2C and links sovereign default hazard rates to the
15:545:41987:14:40:90:204:392:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:FX Poisson arrival rate.
15:546:42011:40:33:90:203:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.1    Pricing kernel
15:547:42032:33:13:90:521:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Suppose,Mt,t+1is the USD-denominated nominal pricing kernel.  We can value a cash flow,
15:548:42119:13:14:89:521:306:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:B:Xt+1, using the pricing kernel viaEt(Mt,t+1Xt+1),where the expectation is computed under

16:566:42883:0:32:90:206:691:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.2    CDS valuation
16:567:42903:32:13:90:522:659:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  start  with  valuation,  as  it  allows  us  to  introduce  the  key  objects  that  we  model  in
16:568:43005:13:14:90:522:646:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:subsequent sections.  A CDS contract with time to maturityThas two legs.  The premium
16:569:43090:14:13:90:522:632:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:leg pays the annual CDS premiumCt,Tuntil a default takes place at a random timeτ.  It

16:572:43347:24:13:90:522:581:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Accordingly, the present value of fixed payments of the USD-denominated contract that a

17:614:45047:40:33:90:185:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.3    Credit risk

17:624:45505:26:13:90:515:386:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f8:B:We assume thatwtconsists ofGglobal andKregional factors, so that each intensityh∗kt
17:625:45588:13:14:90:522:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is a function of all global factors and one of the regional factors.  We assume thatG= 1
17:626:45676:14:13:90:522:359:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:andK= 2 in our empirical work,  implying two factors per country (one global and one
17:627:45760:13:14:90:522:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regional;  by  assumption,  Germany  is  exposed  to  the  global  factor  only,  as  in  Ang  and
17:628:45858:14:13:90:522:332:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Longstaff, 2013).  This choice is motivated by a principal component analysis (PCA) that
17:629:45946:13:14:90:522:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:extracts country-specific components from the quanto spreads.  The procedure implies that
17:630:46035:14:14:90:522:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:two factors explain around 99% of the variation in quanto spreads.  Furthermore, the PCA
17:631:46123:14:13:90:522:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the combination of the first two components across all countries implies that the first
17:632:46213:13:25:90:333:278:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:principal component explains 58% of the variation.
17:633:46263:25:14:90:522:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To gain intuition about how our model of contagion works, consider the Poisson arrival of
17:634:46352:14:13:90:522:239:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:credit  events  at  a  conditional  rate  ofdt.We  would  like  the  realization  from  this  process

17:636:46550:14:25:89:185:212:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f6:C:P|dt∼Poisson(dt).

17:641:46917:25:13:89:521:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In this respect, such a Poisson process can be viewed as an analytically tractable approx-
17:642:47007:13:0:89:521:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:imation to a Bernoulli distribution that is more appropriate for a credit event in a single
18:643:47100:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:country.  For reasons of parsimony, we use this process to count all contemporaneous events
18:644:47191:14:26:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:across the countries in our sample.  Thus, a Poisson model is a better fit for our framework.

19:687:49671:14:26:90:370:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quite modest and similar to the regular innovations in FX.
19:688:49729:26:13:90:522:651:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We link jumps in the FX to the sovereign default risk by assuming that the FX rate jumps
19:689:49817:13:14:90:522:638:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:only in case of a credit event.  Therefore, the FX jump intensity is equal to the sum of all

19:704:50002:46:14:90:522:553:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our assumptions about the constant mean of the FX jump and the link of its intensity to
19:705:50089:14:13:90:522:539:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:default  intensities  are  likely  to  be  oversimplifications  of  reality.   Ideally,  one  would  want
19:706:50194:13:14:90:522:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to separate jumps into default-related and default-unrelated components.  Within the first
19:707:50284:14:13:90:522:512:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:category, one would want to model country-specific links, both in terms of jump intensity
19:708:50373:13:14:90:522:499:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  jump  mean.   While  it  is  certainly  possible  to  specify  a  model  like  that,  it  would  be
19:709:50477:14:13:90:522:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:impossible to estimate such a model with any reasonable degree of precision. That is because
19:710:50569:13:14:90:522:472:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:all these refinements pertain to rare events that are difficult to pin down empirically even
19:711:50661:14:25:90:252:458:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:if they are identified theoretically.
19:712:50698:25:14:90:522:433:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:This connection between jump intensity and country-specific default intensities allows us
19:713:50787:14:14:90:522:419:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to identify the LGD,L.The USD CDS contracts are informative only about the products
19:714:50870:14:13:89:521:405:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:Lh∗ktand, therefore, their sum overk(e.g., Duffie and Singleton,1999).  The quanto feature
19:715:50960:13:14:90:522:392:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:brings in information about the risk-neutral distribution of exchange rates, which does not
19:716:51051:14:13:90:522:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:depend on the LGD. This allows us to identifyλ∗t.Given our identification assumption that
19:717:51140:13:0:90:420:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:links currency jumps to credit events,  we can recoverLby dividing
