23:884:58072:42:32:90:185:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.9    Risk prices
23:885:58090:32:14:90:522:429:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We have articulated all of the modeling components that are needed for security valuation.
23:886:58180:14:13:90:522:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To estimate the model, we need the behavior of state variables under the true probability
23:887:58269:13:14:90:521:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of outcomes.  AppendixDdemonstrates that there exists a pricing kernel that supports a
23:888:58355:14:13:90:522:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:flexible change in the distribution of variables involved in the valuation of securities.  Most
23:889:58450:13:14:90:522:375:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:parameters could be different under the two probabilities.  One may recover the evolution of
23:890:58542:14:13:90:521:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:state variables under the objective probability by dropping the asterisks∗in the expressions
23:891:58634:13:26:90:157:348:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of Section3.5.
23:892:58648:26:14:90:522:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Given the focus on credit events,  we highlight how the prices of default risk work in our
23:893:58738:14:13:90:521:308:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:model.  All of the variables that are related to credit events have true (hkt, λt) and risk-
23:894:58830:13:14:90:521:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:adjusted  (h∗kt, λ∗t)  versions  because  the  event  risk  premium  could  be  time  varying.   In
23:895:58929:14:13:90:522:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:particular,  the  true  and  risk-adjusted  counterparts  may  have  a  different  functional  form
23:896:59028:13:14:90:522:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and a different factor structure.  In addition, each of these variables may have different true
23:897:59123:14:13:90:522:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and risk-adjusted distributions that are related to the respective distributions of the factors
23:898:59218:13:26:90:168:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that drive them.
23:899:59234:26:13:90:521:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  risk-adjusted  and  true  distributions  ofh∗ktandλ∗tcan  be  identified  from  the  cross-
23:900:59330:13:14:90:519:202:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f8:B:section  and  time  series  of  quanto  spreads,  respectively.   The  true  event  frequencieshkt
23:901:59428:14:13:90:522:188:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:andλtcan be identified only from the realized credit events themselves – a challenge for
23:902:59516:13:14:90:522:175:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:financial assets of high credit quality.  As mentioned earlier, we circumvent this difficulty
23:903:59609:14:14:90:522:161:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by associating credit events with extreme movements in quanto spreads.  Even in this case,
23:904:59699:14:13:90:522:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:however,  the  empirical  problem  is  quite  challenging,  so  we  only  model  common  events
23:905:59794:13:14:90:522:134:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and assume that they are directed by the same factors as their risk-adjusted counterparts:
23:906:59884:14:0:90:390:120:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:dt|wt∼ARG0( ̄h+δ>wwt+δddt−1,ρ), andλt=E(dt|wt,dt−1).
24:907:59938:0:33:90:220:691:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.10    Implementation
24:908:59960:33:14:90:522:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We jointly use data on the USD/EUR FX rate, forward FX rates, the term structure of OIS
24:909:60047:14:13:90:522:644:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interest rates, the term structures of CDS quanto spreads for a cross section of six countries,
24:910:60142:13:14:90:522:631:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a cross-section of credit events for six countries, and some data on Greece to estimate the
24:911:60233:14:13:90:521:617:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:model.  The model is estimated using Bayesian MCMC. See AppendixE. The outputs of
24:912:60314:13:14:90:522:604:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the procedure are the state variables and parameter estimates.  We outline the parameter
24:913:60402:14:25:90:222:590:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:restrictions that we impose.
24:914:60430:25:14:90:522:565:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We make the following identifying restrictions.  For the model of the OIS term structure, we
24:915:60522:14:13:90:521:551:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:followDai and Singleton(2000) andHamilton and Wu(2012) and restrictμu= 0, Σu=I,
24:916:60601:13:14:90:521:538:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:δu1≥0, Φ∗ulower triangular with real eigenvalues andφ∗u11≥φ∗u22.For the credit model,
24:917:60686:14:13:90:522:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we impose the mean of the state variablesgtto be equal to 1 under the true probability
24:918:60772:13:14:90:522:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:to avoid scaling indeterminacy.  This implies restrictions on parametersci:ciνi= 1−φ>iι,
24:919:60860:14:14:89:522:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whereιis a vector of ones.  By the same logic, we setρ= 1 in the true dynamics of the
24:920:60945:14:25:89:182:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:contagion factordt.
24:921:60964:25:14:89:521:458:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Because of the large number of parameters, we also impose over-identification restrictions.
24:922:61055:14:13:89:521:444:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  allow  the  global  credit  factorw1tto  affect  regional  factors,  but  not  vice-versa.   This
24:923:61156:13:14:90:521:431:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:restriction affects elementsφi.  We assume the volatility factorvtto be autonomous under
24:924:61244:14:13:89:521:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:both probabilities.  Both sets of restrictions translate into identical restrictions under the
24:925:61338:13:14:89:521:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk-adjusted probability because of the functional form of the risk prices for these factors.
24:926:61432:14:13:89:521:390:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Furthermore,  we  assume  that  the  contagion  factordtloads  only  onw1tunder  the  true
24:927:61522:13:47:90:144:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:probability.
24:928:61534:47:36:90:166:330:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:4    Results
24:929:61546:36:33:90:256:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:4.1    Model selection and fit
24:930:61576:33:13:90:521:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:A table in AppendixF displays the estimated parameters of the OIS term structure.  The
24:931:61662:13:14:90:522:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:model is standard and the parameter values are in line with the literature.  It is difficult
24:932:61754:14:14:90:522:234:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to interpret the model because there are multiple equivalent rotations of the factors.  The
24:933:61845:14:13:90:521:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:key for this paper, as indicated in Table3, is that the pricing errors are reasonably small.
24:934:61937:13:14:90:522:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Therefore, we can use the model to discount cash flows using the risk-adjusted valuation
24:935:62025:14:25:90:129:193:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:method.
24:936:62032:25:14:90:522:168:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We estimate two versions of the credit model:  with and without contagion.  We present the
24:937:62122:14:13:90:522:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimated parameters in AppendixF. There are common traits to the parameter estimates
24:938:62207:13:14:90:521:141:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regardless  of  the  model.   The  factorswtexhibit  near  unit-root  dynamics  under  the  risk-
24:939:62304:14:13:90:522:127:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:adjusted probability, a common trait of affine models.  Under the true probability, only the
24:940:62396:13:0:90:296:114:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:global credit factorw1tis highly persistent.
25:941:62442:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Furthermore, the peripheral countries in our sample have a much larger weight on the global
25:942:62533:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:credit factor than the core countries.  France has a smaller loading on the core credit factor
25:943:62627:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:than Belgium (Germany’s weight is zero by assumption).  Spain’s weight on the peripheral
25:944:62715:13:25:90:454:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:factor is larger than that of Italy and Greece, and similar to that of Ireland.
25:945:62794:25:14:90:521:625:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The loss-given-default parameter,L, is estimated at 41% in the model without contagion,
25:946:62881:14:13:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with a 90% confidence interval of 35% to 50%.  As a reference point, in CDS valuation, it is
25:947:62973:13:14:90:522:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:commonly assumed that this value is 60% for corporate and 75% for EM sovereign bonds.
25:948:63058:14:14:90:522:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The most comparable estimated numbers are provided inPan and Singleton(2008) at 23%
25:949:63141:14:13:90:522:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for Mexico and Turkey, and 83% for South Korea.  We guess that our estimate would have
25:950:63227:13:14:90:521:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:been lower for core countries, asLis affected by events in the periphery (according to the
25:951:63317:14:25:90:362:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Greek CDS settlement auction, the true loss was 78.5%).
25:952:63372:25:13:90:522:518:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We find that the expected depreciation rate does not load on credit factors under either
25:953:63460:13:14:90:522:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:probability, and that the same goes for shocks.  The loading of the expected depreciation
25:954:63549:14:13:90:522:491:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rate on the variance factor is positive under the true probability and negative under the
25:955:63638:13:14:90:522:478:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk-adjusted  one.   This  implies  that,  ignoring  jumps,  the  EUR  is  expected  to  appreci-
25:956:63736:14:25:90:344:464:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ate/depreciate under the corresponding probabilities.
25:957:63789:25:14:90:522:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The FX jump magnitude is just under 1% under the true probability.  This is consistent with
25:958:63880:14:13:90:521:425:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the visually mild observed movements in Figure3B. Under the risk-adjusted probability, it
25:959:63969:13:14:90:522:412:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is 14% implying a huge risk premium associated with currency devaluation upon a sovereign
25:960:64058:14:25:90:149:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:credit event.
25:961:64071:25:14:90:522:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  evaluate  whether  a  larger  model  with  contagion  is  supported  by  the  evidence.   The
25:962:64168:14:13:90:522:359:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:parameters  that  are  contagion-specific,δ∗kd,δd,andρ∗are  statistically  significant.   The
25:963:64261:13:14:90:522:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:question is whether the extra degrees of freedom associated with a larger model are justi-
25:964:64351:14:13:90:522:332:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fied from the statistical and economic perspectives.  While we find some credence for the
25:965:64440:13:14:90:522:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:contagion mechanism in our sample, the improvement in the model’s fit does not justify the
25:966:64530:14:25:90:302:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:associated increase in statistical uncertainty.
25:967:64577:25:14:90:521:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Specifically,  a  table  in  AppendixFreports  the  distributions  of  the  likelihoods  of  both
25:968:64674:14:13:90:522:266:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:models,  and  the  associated  BICs  (the  negative  of  the  likelihood  plus  the  penalty  for  the
25:969:64776:13:14:90:522:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:number of parameters).  Both statistics indicate that the difference between the two models
25:970:64867:14:13:90:521:239:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is insignificant.  Table3 reports various measures of pricing errors for the model without
25:971:64957:13:14:90:522:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:contagion.  The same metrics for the model with contagion are similar and, therefore, are
25:972:65046:14:25:90:522:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not reported for brevity.  Thus, we discuss only the model without contagion in the sequel.
25:973:65137:25:14:90:522:187:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Continuing with Table3 we see that the overall fit is good, with the RMSE ranging from
25:974:65223:14:13:89:521:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2 to 12 basis points.  To visualize the fit, we plot the time series of the observed and fitted
25:975:65318:13:25:89:401:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spreads in Figure4.  The overall high quality of the fit is evident.
25:976:65386:25:14:89:521:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:As a final and out-of-sample test of the model’s quality, we take the estimated factors and
25:977:65477:14:13:89:521:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:re-estimate only the country-specific parameters of the default intensities using data for the
25:978:65571:13:0:89:522:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:remaining 10 countries.  The resulting fit is displayed in Figure5.  The overall quality of the
26:979:65668:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fit remains high,  suggesting that our model is quite reasonable.  The selection procedure
26:980:65758:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the main sample implies that these countries represent less liquid markets.  Therefore,
26:981:65848:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fitting these quanto spreads perfectly is not required.  The observed spreads for Cyprus are
26:982:65940:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quite erratic, manifesting the illiquidity and riskiness of this sovereign, so the fit here is the
26:983:66038:14:38:90:119:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:worst.
26:984:66044:38:30:90:241:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:4.2    Default probabilities
26:985:66072:30:30:90:166:568:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Credit factors
26:986:66086:30:14:90:521:538:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure 6 displays the filtered credit factorswt.  Recall that one of the identifying restrictions
26:987:66183:14:14:90:522:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is that the means of these factors are set to 1.  This explains the similarity in scale.  The
26:988:66276:14:13:90:522:510:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:time-series patterns are quite different.  All factors exhibit large movements in 2012, around
26:989:66370:13:14:90:522:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  height  of  the  sovereign  debt  crisis.   This  period  was  marked  by  the  downgrades  of
26:990:66469:14:13:90:522:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:individual  sovereigns,  the  creation  of  the  European  Financial  Stability  Facility,  and  the
26:991:66569:13:14:90:522:470:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:political instability in Greece.  The crisis reached its peak when Greece officially defaulted
26:992:66663:14:13:90:522:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  March  2012.   The  sharp  drop  in  the  factors  shortly  thereafter  is  associated  with  the
26:993:66764:13:14:90:522:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:famous speech by Mario Draghi in July 2012, vowing to do “whatever it takes” to save the
26:994:66852:14:23:90:356:429:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:EUR. All of the factors persistently decrease thereafter.
26:995:66909:23:14:90:522:406:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The peripheral factorw3t, associated with Italy, Ireland, and Spain, also exhibits substantial
26:996:67003:14:13:90:522:392:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variation prior to 2012 and, to a lesser degree, for the rest of the sample period.  The core
26:997:67096:13:14:90:521:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:factorw2t,  which corresponds to Belgium and France,  starts to pick up shortly after the
26:998:67185:14:13:90:522:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:marked increase in the periphery factorw3t, but much earlier than the pronounced increase
26:999:67274:13:14:90:521:352:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the common factorw1t.  Interestingly,w1tpicks up again at the very end of the sample
26:1000:67361:14:38:90:123:338:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:period.
26:1001:67368:38:30:90:343:300:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Time series of risk-adjusted default intensities
26:1002:67416:30:13:90:522:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Various combinations of these factors deliver risk-adjusted default intensities for the respec-
26:1003:67511:13:14:90:522:257:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tive countries via Equation (6).  Figure7A displays these intensities.  Given the common
26:1004:67599:14:14:90:522:243:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variation  in  credit  factors  during  2012,  it  is  not  surprising  to  see  elevated  default  prob-
26:1005:67704:14:13:90:522:229:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:abilities  during  that  period,  irrespective  of  the  country.   The  largest  one-period  default
26:1006:67805:13:14:90:522:216:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:probability is almost 2.5% (default probabilities are approximately equal to intensities for
26:1007:67897:14:13:90:522:202:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:such small numbers).  Ireland, Italy, and Spain have clearly distinct patterns of intensities
26:1008:67990:13:14:90:522:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the post-2012 period, a manifestation of their exposure to the factorw3t.  The same three
26:1009:68082:14:13:90:522:175:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:countries exhibit some elevation at the end of 2016 – a result of their extensive exposure to
26:1010:68175:13:14:90:522:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the global factor, which also picks up.  Overall, Spain is the riskiest county.  Germany does
26:1011:68268:14:13:90:522:148:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not load on the regional components at all.  Hence, Germany has the lowest default risk,
26:1012:68356:13:14:90:522:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and its dynamic properties are distinct from those of other countries.  These differences in
26:1013:68448:14:13:90:522:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:dynamics manifest themselves in the differences between the average quanto curves that we
26:1014:68537:13:0:90:175:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:noted in Figure3.
27:1015:68556:0:33:90:353:691:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Cross-section of risk-adjusted default intensities
27:1016:68606:33:14:90:522:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Table  4  summarizes  how  the  default  intensities  of  all  countries,  including  the  10  out-of-
27:1017:68708:14:13:90:522:644:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:samples ones, load on the factors.  The countries are sorted by their loadings on the global
27:1018:68800:13:14:90:521:631:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:credit factor,δ∗kw1.  Germany is roughly in the middle.  Spain has the largest exposure at
27:1019:68890:14:25:90:418:617:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:four times that of Germany, and Finland the smallest at 14−1times.
27:1020:68956:25:14:90:522:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Overall,  the  countries  exhibit  large  cross-sectional  variation  in  their  exposure  to  credit
27:1021:69057:14:13:90:522:578:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:factors.  Among the core countries, Belgium and France have a sizable exposure to the core
27:1022:69147:13:14:90:522:565:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:factor, while others have nearly zero exposure.  Finland appears to be the safest country
27:1023:69236:14:25:90:338:551:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with tiny exposures to both global and core factors.
27:1024:69288:25:14:90:522:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:On the peripheral side, the relatively recent additions to the Eurozone, such as Estonia and
27:1025:69380:14:13:90:522:512:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Slovakia, have a tiny exposure to region-specific risk, so they are largely indistinguishable
27:1026:69473:13:14:90:522:499:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from some core countries, including Germany itself.  The Southern European countries have
27:1027:69562:14:25:90:434:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a large regional component.  Spain and Greece stand out in this respect.
27:1028:69634:25:14:90:522:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Eurozone quanto spreads are driven by common variation in the exchange rate and mon-
27:1029:69718:14:14:90:522:446:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:etary policy.  Thus, cross-country differences in model-implied default intensities ought to
27:1030:69810:14:13:90:522:432:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be related to cross-country differences in fiscal health.  To test that conjecture, we collect
27:1031:69904:13:14:90:522:419:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:information on quarterly debt-to-GDP and FX reserves-to-debt ratios and relate them to
27:1032:69990:14:13:90:522:405:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the model-implied hazard rates.  We source these data from the Bank for International Set-
27:1033:70080:13:14:90:522:392:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tlements and the International Monetary Fund International Financial Statistics database.
27:1034:70169:14:13:90:522:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The data span is from the start of our sample, that is, the third quarter of 2010, up to the
27:1035:70261:13:26:90:439:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:second quarter of 2015.  All data are measured in USD for comparability.
27:1036:70333:26:13:90:522:339:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  report  the  relation  between  these  fiscal  variables  and  model-implied  hazard  rates  in
27:1037:70432:13:14:90:522:326:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Table 5.  The relation between debt-to-GDP and hazard rates is positive and statistically
27:1038:70521:14:13:90:522:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:significant at the 1% level, with anR2of 13% for this univariate regression.  The coefficient
27:1039:70614:13:14:90:522:299:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of 0.20 implies that a one percentage point increase in a country’s debt-to-GDP ratio (+0.01)
27:1040:70707:14:14:90:522:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is on average associated with an 0.002 increase in intensity. This is economically meaningful.
27:1041:70801:14:13:90:522:271:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:If hazard rates are constant,  CDS premiums may be approximated byL·h∗t.  Given the
27:1042:70884:13:26:90:506:258:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimatedLof 41%, this implies an increase in CDS premiums of approximately 8 bps.
27:1043:70966:26:13:90:522:232:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:For the specification in column (2), we add time fixed effects to further absorb any remaining
27:1044:71060:13:14:90:522:219:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:common variation in hazard rates.  Given the strong factor structure in CDS premiums in
27:1045:71147:14:13:90:522:205:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our model, this adjustment should absorb a significant amount of cross-sectional variation.
27:1046:71238:13:14:90:522:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:TheR2increases to 44%, and the regression coefficient is stable, suggesting a meaningful
27:1047:71326:14:13:90:522:178:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cross-sectional relation between the model-implied hazard rates and each country’s fiscal
27:1048:71415:13:26:90:123:165:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:health.
27:1049:71422:26:13:90:522:139:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:As an alternative measure of fiscal health, we use a country’s foreign exchange rate reserves
27:1050:71515:13:14:90:522:126:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to debt outstanding in columns (3) and (4).  The negative regression coefficient implies that
27:1051:71608:14:0:90:522:112:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:countries that have debt that is better collateralized by foreign exchange rate reserves have
28:1052:71703:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lower hazard rates.  The economic effect is smaller.  WithL= 0.41, the coefficient of−0.03
28:1053:71793:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:implies a 1 bps lower CDS premium for each additional percentage point in FX reserves
28:1054:71878:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relative to debt outstanding.  The coefficient is unaltered if we absorb additional common
28:1055:71968:13:26:90:329:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variation through time fixed effects in column (4).
28:1056:72019:26:13:90:522:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We examine the joint effect of both fiscal variables in columns (5) and (6).  Debt-to-GDP
28:1057:72108:13:14:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:appears to be the driving variable.  Its coefficient remains stable and significant at the 1%
28:1058:72201:14:40:90:114:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:level.
28:1059:72207:40:33:90:208:557:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Credit risk premiums
28:1060:72227:33:14:90:522:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:While  we  cannot  characterize  the  default  risk  premiums  for  individual  countries,  we  can
28:1061:72326:14:13:90:522:510:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:do so for the overall credit risk.  Figure7B displays the aggregate true and risk-adjusted
28:1062:72416:13:14:90:522:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:default intensitiesλtandλ∗t, respectively. We show them on different scales because the true
28:1063:72508:14:13:90:522:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:default intensity is much smaller.  Visually, they track each other quite closely, suggesting
28:1064:72601:13:14:90:522:470:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a constant risk premium.  However, this is not the case.  To illustrate this, we characterize
28:1065:72694:14:13:90:522:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the corresponding risk premium, in line with the literature, viaλ∗t/λt,displayed in Figure
28:1066:72784:13:26:90:106:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:7C.
28:1067:72787:26:13:90:522:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:On  average,  this  number  is  1.95,  and  is  drifting  downward  toward  the  end  of  the  sam-
28:1068:72886:13:14:90:522:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ple.  Starting from 2014, the premium is insignificantly different from 1.  As a benchmark,
28:1069:72977:14:13:90:521:390:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Driessen(2005) assumes a constant default premium in the context of corporate debt and
28:1070:73063:13:14:90:522:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates  it  to  be  2.3.   Combining  CDS-implied  default  intensities  with  Moody’s  KMV
28:1071:73157:14:14:90:522:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expected  default  frequencies,Berndt,  Douglas,  Duffie,  and  Ferguson(2018)  also  find  an
28:1072:73251:14:13:90:522:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:average default premia of around 2 for a sample of 93 firms in three industries.  The ra-
28:1073:73340:13:14:90:522:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tios of risk-adjusted to true default intensities, however, exhibit substantial time variation,
28:1074:73435:14:25:90:171:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between 1 and 6.
28:1075:73451:25:14:90:521:297:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Bai, Collin-Dufresne, Goldstein, and Helwege(2015) andGouri ́eroux, Monfort, and Renne
28:1076:73537:14:13:90:522:283:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(2014) emphasize that if a model of default intensity is missing the contagion effect, then
28:1077:73628:13:14:90:522:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the ratio of intensities might be overstating the true premium for credit risk.  In our case,
28:1078:73721:14:13:90:522:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a version of the model with contagion generates an average premium of 2 and by and large
28:1079:73809:13:42:90:173:243:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:similar dynamics.
28:1080:73826:42:32:90:406:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:4.3    Devaluation contingent on default – the twin Ds
28:1081:73880:32:33:90:152:169:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Probability
28:1082:73891:33:13:90:522:136:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The estimation results allow us to weigh in on the debate about whether default has an
28:1083:73977:13:14:90:522:123:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:immediate or long-term impact on the exchange rate.Krugman(1979) suggests that default
28:1084:74063:14:0:90:522:109:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:leads  to  a  change  in  the  drift  of  the  depreciation  rate,  with  a  persistent  and  continuous
29:1085:74169:0:14:90:521:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:depreciation of the local currency.  Na, Schmitt-Groh ́e, Uribe, and Yue(2017), in contrast,
29:1086:74261:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:argue that the FX rate suffers a significant one-time drop upon default.  See our discussion
29:1087:74353:14:24:90:191:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:around Equation (8).
29:1088:74373:24:14:90:522:639:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The aforementioned lack of a significant effect of credit factors on the expected depreciation
29:1089:74467:14:13:90:522:625:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rate  implies  that  default  is  unlikely  to  have  a  long-term  effect  on  currencies.   Thus,  the
29:1090:74571:13:14:90:522:612:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimation results imply that changes in the FX rate are linked to credit risk only through
29:1091:74662:14:13:90:522:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:jumps.  The jump component is significant, implying an acute and short-term interaction
29:1092:74749:13:25:90:195:585:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between the Twin Ds.
29:1093:74769:25:13:90:522:560:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:How likely is the EUR to devalue if one of the sovereigns in the Eurozone defaults?  The
29:1094:74857:13:14:90:522:547:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:answer requires a more formal definition of devaluation.  We associate it with an extreme
29:1095:74946:14:13:90:522:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:movement in exchange rates, and rely on our model to measure the probability of such an
29:1096:75033:13:14:90:522:520:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:event.  Specifically, we define the EUR devaluation as a drop inStthat is larger than three
29:1097:75124:14:24:90:243:506:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conditional standard deviations.
29:1098:75156:24:14:90:522:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The model implies that the true 1-week probability of devaluation conditional on default
29:1099:75244:14:13:90:522:468:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is  4.64%.   The  risk-adjusted  probability  of  devaluation  conditional  on  default  is  76.60%,
29:1100:75344:13:14:90:522:455:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:suggesting a large risk premium for this event.  We will quantify this premium directly in
29:1101:75434:14:14:90:522:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the next section.  The true 1-year probability is 0.02%, which is smaller than the 1-week
29:1102:75523:14:13:90:522:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:probability.  Thus, devaluation comes primarily through a sharp, short-term decline in the
29:1103:75613:13:14:90:522:414:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:EUR. This decline in probabilities with the horizon is consistent with a one-off impact of
29:1104:75703:14:13:90:522:400:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:default on the FX rate, as discussed above.  This number is also much smaller than those
29:1105:75791:13:14:90:522:387:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reported byNa, Schmitt-Groh ́e, Uribe, and Yue(2017) andReinhart(2002).  Part of this
29:1106:75876:14:13:90:522:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:difference may be explained by the sample (developed versus emerging economies), and by
29:1107:75963:13:14:90:522:360:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our primary use of market data, rather than realized defaults.  The corresponding 1-year
29:1108:76051:14:24:90:432:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk-adjusted probability of devaluation conditional on default is 0.85%.
29:1109:76124:24:14:90:522:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We also measure the sensitivity of the probability of devaluation to changes in the prob-
29:1110:76213:14:13:90:522:308:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ability of default, which we represent by the default intensity.  We can view the previous
29:1111:76303:13:14:90:522:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:exercise  as  a  particular  case  in  which  the  default  intensity  is  equal  to  infinity.   Over  the
29:1112:76410:14:14:90:522:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:1-week horizon, the true (risk-adjusted) devaluation probability increases by 0.04% (0.73%)
29:1113:76501:14:13:90:522:267:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for every 1% increase in the default intensity.  The small sensitivity of the true probability is
29:1114:76598:13:14:90:522:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a manifestation of the small jump size.  Thus, a large increase in the intensity is needed for
29:1115:76692:14:13:90:522:240:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the jump component to affect devaluation.  Figure7B shows that the largest movement in
29:1116:76778:13:14:90:522:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the true (risk-adjusted) default intensity was equal to 0.5% (6.7%), which occurred between
29:1117:76869:14:13:90:522:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:December 2011 and June 2012 during the Eurozone debt crisis.  This increase translates
29:1118:76955:13:14:90:522:200:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:into an increase of 0.02% (4.9%) in the true (risk-adjusted) probability of devaluation.  Over
29:1119:77049:14:13:90:522:186:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:1 year, the devaluation sensitivities to default are 0% (under true probability) and 0.04%
29:1120:77139:13:14:90:522:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(risk-adjusted probability).  This decline is consistent with the aforementioned short-term
29:1121:77230:14:24:90:241:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effect of default on devaluation.
29:1122:77263:24:14:90:522:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Overall, the probability of devaluation related to default is modest under the true proba-
29:1123:77353:14:13:90:522:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bility.  Yet, the risk-adjusted counterparts are rather high.  This suggests the occurrence of
29:1124:77447:13:0:90:522:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:currency devaluation during particularly bad states of the economy that tend to coincide
30:1125:77537:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with a high marginal utility of the representative agent.  This interpretation is similar to the
30:1126:77633:14:14:90:521:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:equilibrium models ofAugustin and T ́edongap(2016) andChernov, Schmid, and Schneider
30:1127:77717:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(2017), who characterize the large risk premia demanded by risk-sensitive investors for sell-
30:1128:77810:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ing CDS protection on sovereigns in developed economies.  In the next section, we directly
30:1129:77900:14:39:90:447:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:measure the risk premiums associated with default-contingent devaluation.
30:1130:77973:39:31:90:173:597:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Risk premiums
30:1131:77986:31:13:90:522:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We start with the case that ignores the timing of default, and compute both the risk-adjusted
30:1132:78079:13:14:90:522:553:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expectation of the depreciation rate,E∗t[ST/St], and its true counterpart,Et[ST/St].The
30:1133:78166:14:13:90:521:539:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:first row of Figure8 shows that the true expectations indicate expected EUR devaluation,
30:1134:78254:13:14:90:522:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the average term structure of such expectations is downward sloping (EUR is expected
30:1135:78342:14:13:90:522:512:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to devalue more at longer horizons).  The risk-adjusted expectation shows that the USD is
30:1136:78431:13:24:90:383:499:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expected to devalue, on average, at horizons of up to 3 years.
30:1137:78493:24:14:90:521:475:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To  understand  this  result,  consider  covered  interest  parity,  which  impliesE∗t[ST/St]  =
30:1138:78589:14:14:90:522:461:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:Ft,T/St=  exp[(T−t)(yt,T−̂yt,T)]  witĥyt,Tdenoting  the  EUR  benchmark  yield.   Thus,
30:1139:78677:14:13:90:522:447:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the expectation is positive wheneveryt,T>̂yt,T.The displayed relationship is thus pinned
30:1140:78765:13:24:90:416:434:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:down by the currency forward ratesFt,Tthat we used in estimation.
30:1141:78830:24:14:90:522:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:One   implication   is   that   we   observe   the   standard   currency   premium   relationship,
30:1142:78928:14:13:90:521:396:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:EtST/E∗tST,often expressed as the carry trade.  Borrowing in the high-interest rate USD,
30:1143:79016:13:14:90:522:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:converting to EUR, and then lending in this currency, leads, on average, to negative (log)
30:1144:79106:14:13:90:522:369:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:excess returns at short horizons.  At long horizons (log) excess returns are not significantly
30:1145:79200:13:14:90:522:356:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:different  from  zero,  consistent  with  the  evidence  inLustig,  Stathopoulos,  and  Verdelhan
30:1146:79297:14:24:90:123:342:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(2016).
30:1147:79304:24:13:90:522:318:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The second row of Figure8 includes a condition on the timingτof any credit event rather
30:1148:79391:13:14:90:521:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:than the one in a specific country.  In this case, the arrival rate is controlled byλt, and we
30:1149:79485:14:14:90:522:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:can compute both the risk-adjusted expectation and its true counterpart.  Default risk has
30:1150:79575:14:13:90:522:277:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:almost no impact in the short-term, so the plot forT= 1 year is similar to that for the no-
30:1151:79666:13:14:90:521:264:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:default case (it is literally identical ifT= 1 week).  The level of risk-adjusted expectations
30:1152:79760:14:13:90:522:250:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:moves upwards with longer maturities in this case,  indicating the risk-adjusted expected
30:1153:79849:13:14:90:522:237:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:USD depreciation conditional on default.  This happens because early termination leads to
30:1154:79938:14:24:90:285:223:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a loss in the expected USD appreciation.
30:1155:79978:24:13:90:522:199:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In risk premium terms, we observe a drastic difference in relation to the no-default case.
30:1156:80068:13:14:90:522:186:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Carry returns to EUR are still negative in the short run, and continue to be so as the horizon
30:1157:80162:14:13:90:522:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expands.  That is a manifestation of the interaction with default risk.  No amount of interest
30:1158:80256:13:14:90:522:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:earned on a long-term debt instrument can compensate for currency losses experienced in
30:1159:80343:14:24:90:162:145:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:case of default.
30:1160:80359:24:13:90:522:121:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Indeed,   we  can  quantify  how  much  more  risk  premium  is  required  for  such  a  sce-
30:1161:80452:13:0:90:522:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:nario.    Expressing  risk  premiums  in  logs,  (T−t)−1log[EtST/E∗tST]  (no  default)  and
31:1162:80545:0:14:90:521:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(T−t)−1log[EtSt∧T/E∗tSt∧T]  (default),  we  can  compute  the  difference  between  the  two.
31:1163:80638:14:14:89:521:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:It reflects the extra compensation one earns for the currency loss in case of default, com-
31:1164:80729:14:13:89:521:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pared  with  the  compensation  for  the  regular  currency  risk.   The  third  row  of  Figure8
31:1165:80826:13:26:90:473:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:displays these differences forT= 1 and 5 years, and the average term structure.
31:1166:80905:26:13:90:522:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:At short horizons this “excess risk premium” changes sign sporadically and stabilizes at zero
31:1167:80998:13:14:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:after the sovereign debt crisis.  The average value is slightly positive and corresponds to a
31:1168:81091:14:13:90:522:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:negative extra premium for EUR depreciation. But, as can be seen from the third panel, that
31:1169:81182:13:14:90:522:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:extra premium is not significantly different from zero.  The same average effects persist for
31:1170:81275:14:13:90:522:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:maturities of up to 4 years.2After that, the excess premium for EUR depreciation increases
31:1171:81365:13:14:90:522:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to 0.3% at the 15-year horizon and levels off at 0.5% per week at the 30-year horizon (not
31:1172:81455:14:13:90:522:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:shown).  These numbers are large, and liquidity effects could be, in part, responsible for such
31:1173:81550:13:41:90:520:530:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a magnitude.  But even one half of these premiums would still be economically significant.
31:1174:81640:41:33:90:364:489:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:C:Expected devaluation and relative quanto spreads
31:1175:81688:33:13:90:521:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Several authors, such asDu and Schreger(2016) andMano(2013), use observed relative
31:1176:81770:13:14:89:521:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quanto  spreads,  in  the  context  of  EM,  to  measure  the  anticipated  currency  devaluation
31:1177:81867:14:13:89:521:429:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  case  of  a  credit  event.   As  we  show  in  Equation  (1),  the  relative  spread  consists  of
31:1178:81970:13:14:89:521:416:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:two  components:  the  risk-adjusted  expected  depreciation  conditional  on  default  and  the
31:1179:82066:14:14:89:521:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interaction of default and FX jump.  The second term reflects the propensity of the EUR
31:1180:82153:14:25:89:328:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to depreciate when the default intensity increases.
31:1181:82204:25:14:89:521:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To facilitate the discussion, we switch to the ratio of the local and the foreign currency CDS
31:1182:82298:14:24:89:465:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spreads, which has a more straightforward connection to the depreciation rate,
31:1183:82376:24:18:155:173:325:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:C:Cet,T
31:1184:82381:18:0:155:173:307:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:C:C$t,T
31:1185:82386:0:0:179:202:316:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f8:A:=E∗t
31:1186:82390:0:8:206:212:332:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:[
31:1187:82391:8:15:213:235:324:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:C:Sτ∧T
31:1188:82395:15:0:220:230:309:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:C:St
31:1189:82397:0:16:238:244:332:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:]
31:1190:82398:16:0:246:275:316:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f8:A:+cov∗t
31:1191:82404:0:11:279:285:335:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:[
31:1192:82405:11:16:294:387:324:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:A:e−r(τ∧T−t)I(τ≤T)
31:1193:82421:16:0:287:393:308:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:A:E∗te−r(τ∧T−t)I(τ≤T)
31:1194:82440:0:0:395:398:316:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:C:,
31:1195:82441:0:15:401:423:324:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:C:Sτ∧T
31:1196:82445:15:0:407:417:309:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:C:St
31:1197:82447:0:19:426:432:335:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:]
31:1198:82448:19:33:434:437:316:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:C:.
31:1199:82449:33:14:89:521:283:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:This expression makes it explicit that a direct reading of the data, as expected depreciation
31:1200:82542:14:13:89:521:269:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:upon default,  is prone to be biased, as it may overstate the importance of the impact of
31:1201:82631:13:14:89:521:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sovereign  default  on  the  local  currency  depreciation.   Our  model  allows  us  to  gauge  the
31:1202:82731:14:13:89:521:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relative importance of both terms, both across countries and over time.  We illustrate these
31:1203:82823:13:26:89:221:229:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:decompositions in Figure9.
31:1204:82849:26:13:89:521:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:As  a  start,  focus  on  the  last  column  that  depicts  the  time-averages  of  relative  quanto
31:1205:82949:13:14:89:521:190:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spreads across the term structure for the six countries that we use in the main estimation.
31:1206:83040:14:14:89:521:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The black-circled lines display the observed relative CDS spreads,Cet,T/C$t,T.  If one were
31:1207:83131:14:16:89:521:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to take the view that the spread reflects the risk-adjusted expectation of the depreciation
31:1208:83222:16:14:102:521:146:6:g_d0_f14:9:g_d0_f15:F:2At  first  blush,  this  result  appears  to  be  at  odds  with  the  large  differences  in  true  and  risk-adjusted
31:1209:83342:14:11:90:522:132:9:g_d0_f15:9:g_d0_f15:F:1-week probabilities of devaluation conditional on default that we reported in the previous section.  The risk
31:1210:83452:11:11:90:522:121:9:g_d0_f15:9:g_d0_f15:F:premiums reflect compensation for any adverse movement in EUR. In contrast, the probabilities reflect an
31:1211:83556:11:0:90:326:110:9:g_d0_f15:9:g_d0_f15:F:extreme event of at least a three-standard-deviation move.
32:1212:83616:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rate only, then the Figure would tell us that, for 1-year contracts, the Euro is expected to
32:1213:83708:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:depreciate on average by about 30% for Germany,  28% for France,  up to about 15% for
32:1214:83793:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Ireland.  For longer horizon contracts, the magnitude of the expected impact is increasing.
32:1215:83884:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:For the 5-year maturity, for example, the expected drop in the local currency given default
32:1216:83975:14:25:90:291:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is as large as 44% in the case of Germany.
32:1217:84017:25:14:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The gray lines depict the model-implied default-contingent risk-adjusted expected depreci-
32:1218:84107:14:13:90:522:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ation rateE∗t[Sτ∧T/St].  The gap between the two lines emphasizes that the view of that
32:1219:84194:13:14:89:521:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expectation as the observed relative quanto spread is biased.  Generally, the model-based
32:1220:84283:14:13:89:521:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk-adjusted expectation is above the relative quanto spread implying a negativecov∗tterm
32:1221:84373:13:14:89:521:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the decomposition, on average.  This is intuitive as one would expect the event of default
32:1222:84466:14:13:89:521:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the value of the EUR to move in the opposite directions.  Quantitatively, the difference
32:1223:84558:13:14:89:521:530:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ranges  from  a  high  of  27%  for  Germany  to  a  low  of  10%  for  Ireland  at  short  horizons,
32:1224:84659:14:14:89:521:516:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and declines at longer horizons.  The decline suggests that market participants perceive the
32:1225:84751:14:25:89:416:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sensitivity of the FX rate to default risk to weaken in the long-term.
32:1226:84821:25:14:89:521:477:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The cross-country variation in thecov∗tterm suggests that the impact of a credit even in
32:1227:84909:14:13:89:521:463:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:one  of  the  core  countries  is  more  important  than  that  in  the  peripheral  ones.   The  time
32:1228:85011:13:14:89:521:450:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:series plots of relative quanto spreads and expected depreciation rates at different horizons,
32:1229:85105:14:13:89:522:436:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the first three columns of Figure9, convey more detail about this observation.  We focus
32:1230:85196:13:14:89:521:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on the 5-year horizon in the second column.  The gap between the gray and black lines is
32:1231:85284:14:13:89:521:409:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:increasing in the build-up of the European debt crisis in 2011 and 2012.  This suggests that
32:1232:85376:13:14:89:521:396:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the covariance risk became of greater importance during that period.  A sharp change of
32:1233:85463:14:13:89:521:382:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:this pattern is visible in July 2012,  when the gap between the two plotted lines narrows
32:1234:85552:13:14:89:521:369:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:significantly in particular for the peripheral countries (Ireland, Italy, and Spain), but not
32:1235:85645:14:14:89:521:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for the core countries (Belgium, France, Germany).  This episode coincides with Draghi’s
32:1236:85733:14:25:89:360:341:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:speech, vowing to do whatever it takes to save the EUR.
32:1237:85788:25:14:89:521:316:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:One  interpretation  of  the  data  is  that  Draghi  was  to  some  extent  successful  in  changing
32:1238:85889:14:13:89:521:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  market’s  perception  about  the  interaction  of  FX  and  default  risks.   This  perception
32:1239:85988:13:14:89:521:289:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:has nearly collapsed to zero for peripheral countries, but not so for core countries.  That
32:1240:86079:14:13:89:521:275:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:difference  highlights  the  systemic  role  of  the  core  countries  and  the  fear  of  the  impact
32:1241:86181:13:14:89:521:262:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of their defaults on the EUR currency,  irrespectively of how unlikely that event may be.
32:1242:86270:14:13:89:521:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Consequently, markets may still expect a sell-off of the EUR in the case of default.  Cross-
32:1243:86362:13:14:89:521:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:country  differences  over  time  consistently  suggest  that  Germany  is  expected  to  have  the
32:1244:86461:14:46:89:365:221:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:greatest impact on the exchange rate if it were to default.
32:1245:86520:46:37:89:190:175:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:5    Conclusion
32:1246:86535:37:13:89:521:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Sovereign CDS quanto spreads offer a market perspective on the Twin Ds.  We study their
32:1247:86622:13:14:89:521:125:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interactions and the corresponding risk premiums from an asset pricing perspective.  To that
32:1248:86714:14:0:89:521:111:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:end, we propose an affine no-arbitrage model of the joint dynamics of the quanto spreads
33:1249:86804:0:14:90:522:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of 17 Eurozone countries and the USD/EUR exchange rate.  Controlling for exchange rate
33:1250:86890:14:14:90:522:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk,  credit  risk  has  a  parsimonious  three-factor  structure  (global,  core,  and  peripheral),
33:1251:86992:14:13:90:522:663:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:indicating a lot of common movement.  Cross-country differences in credit risk are related
33:1252:87082:13:14:90:522:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to a measure of debt, indicating the connection between cross-sectional variation in default
33:1253:87174:14:25:90:256:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:risk and variation in fiscal policies.
33:1254:87212:25:14:90:522:611:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  find  that  the  probability  of  devaluation  conditional  on  default  is  low.   But  the  risk
33:1255:87314:14:13:90:522:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:premium for this event is large, much larger than either the credit risk premium or the carry
33:1256:87407:13:14:90:522:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:trade return individually.  These results pinpoint the economic importance of the Twin Ds,
33:1257:87497:14:13:90:522:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as their occurrence coincides with the worst states of the economy when investors’ marginal
33:1258:87588:13:0:90:157:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:utility is high.

52:2125:111079:0:38:90:293:691:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:A    Institutional background
52:2126:111108:38:14:90:522:653:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:CDS contracts are controlled by three documents:  the Credit Derivatives Definitions
52:2127:111192:14:14:90:522:639:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:(“the Definitions”),  the ISDA Credit Derivatives Physical Settlement Matrix (“the
52:2128:111274:14:25:90:510:625:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:Physical Settlement Matrix”), and the Confirmation Letter (“the Confirmation”).
52:2129:111353:25:14:90:522:600:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:The Physical Settlement Matrix is the most important document because the push for
52:2130:111435:14:14:90:522:586:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:standardization has created specific transaction types that are by convention applica-
52:2131:111521:14:14:90:522:572:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:ble to certain types of a sovereign reference entity, e.g., Standard Western European
52:2132:111606:14:14:90:522:558:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:Sovereign  (SWES)  or  Standard  Emerging  European  Sovereign  (SEES)  single-name
52:2133:111689:14:14:90:522:544:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:contracts.  In total,  there are nine transaction types listed in the sovereign section
52:2134:111776:14:14:90:522:530:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:of the Physical Settlement Matrix that contain details about the main contractual
52:2135:111857:14:25:90:420:516:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:provisions for transactions in CDS referencing sovereign entities.
52:2136:111923:25:14:90:522:491:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:Given the over-the-counter (OTC) nature of CDS contracts, parties are free to com-
52:2137:112005:14:14:90:522:477:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:bine features from different transaction types, which would be recognized in the Con-
52:2138:112090:14:14:90:522:463:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:firmation, i.e., the letter that designates the appropriate terms for a CDS contract.
52:2139:112175:14:14:90:522:449:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:The Confirmation,  which is mutually negotiated and drafted between two counter-
52:2140:112255:14:14:90:522:435:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:parties, can thereby amend legal clauses attributed to conventional contract charac-
52:2141:112339:14:14:90:522:421:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:teristics.   Hence,  there  may  be  slight  variations  from  standard  transaction  types  if
52:2142:112434:14:14:90:522:407:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:counterparties agree to alter the terms of conventional CDS contracts.  Such changes
52:2143:112518:14:14:90:522:393:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:introduce  legal  risk,  and  potentially  make  the  contracts  less  liquid,  given  the  cus-
52:2144:112614:14:25:90:337:379:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:tomization required for efficient central clearing.
52:2145:112665:25:14:90:522:354:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:The terms used in the documentation of most credit derivatives transactions are de-
52:2146:112748:14:14:90:522:340:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:fined in the Definitions.  On 22 September 2014,  ISDA introduced the 2014 Credit
52:2147:112829:14:14:90:522:326:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:Derivatives Definitions, which update the 2003 Credit Derivatives Definitions.  We use
52:2148:112915:14:14:90:522:312:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:contracts governed by the 2003 Definitions to guarantee internal consistency through-
52:2149:113000:14:26:90:206:298:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:out our sample period.
52:2150:113022:26:14:90:522:272:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:It  is  important  to  distinguish  between  the  circumstances  under  which  a  CDS  pay-
52:2151:113113:14:13:90:522:258:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:out/credit  event  could  be  triggered,  and  the  restrictions  on  obligations  eligible  for
52:2152:113209:13:14:90:522:245:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:delivery in the settlement process upon the occurrence of a qualifying credit event.
52:2153:113293:14:14:90:522:231:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:The Physical Settlement matrix lays out the credit events that trigger CDS payment,
52:2154:113376:14:14:90:522:217:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:which follows the ruling by a determinations committee of the occurrence of a credit
52:2155:113460:14:14:90:522:203:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:event and a credit event auction.  SWES transaction types recognize three sovereign
52:2156:113543:14:14:90:522:189:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:credit events,  namely Failure to Pay,  Repudiation/Moratorium,  and Restructuring.
52:2157:113626:14:14:90:522:175:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:SEES contracts further list Obligation Acceleration as a valid event that could trigger
52:2158:113713:14:26:90:176:161:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:the CDS payout.
52:2159:113728:26:14:90:522:135:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:The most disputed among all credit events is the Restructuring credit event clause
52:2160:113810:14:13:90:522:121:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:related to a change to the reference obligation that is binding on all holders of the
52:2161:113895:13:0:90:522:108:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:obligation.  The most controversial among such changes is the redenomination of the
53:2162:113980:0:14:90:522:691:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:principal or interest payment into a new currency.  For the credit event to be triggered
53:2163:114068:14:14:90:522:677:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:under the 2014 Definitions, this new currency must be any currency other than the
53:2164:114149:14:14:90:522:663:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:lawful  currency  of  Canada,  Japan,  Switzerland,  the  United  Kingdom,  the  United
53:2165:114236:14:14:90:522:649:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:States of America, and the Euro (or any successor currency to any of the currencies
53:2166:114319:14:14:90:522:635:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:listed; in the case of the Euro, the new currency must replace the Euro in whole).  In
53:2167:114405:14:14:90:522:621:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:the 2003 Definitions, permitted currencies were defined as those of G7 countries and
53:2168:114489:14:26:90:244:607:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:AAA-rated OECD economies.
53:2169:114514:26:14:90:522:581:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:Another important dimension to consider is the obligation category and the associated
53:2170:114599:14:14:90:522:567:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:obligation characteristics which may trigger a credit event.  For SWES contracts, the
53:2171:114684:14:14:90:522:553:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:Obligation category is defined broadly as “borrowed money,” which includes deposits
53:2172:114767:14:14:90:522:539:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:and reimbursement obligations arising from a letter of credit or qualifying guarantees.
53:2173:114854:14:14:90:522:525:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:Such contracts also feature no restrictions on the characteristics of obligations relevant
53:2174:114944:14:14:90:522:511:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:for the triggers of default payment. For SEESs, however, markets have agreed on more
53:2175:115028:14:14:90:522:497:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:specificity for the reference obligations, which encompass only “bonds,” which are not
53:2176:115114:14:14:90:522:483:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:allowed to be subordinated, denominated in domestic currency, issued domestically or
53:2177:115198:14:26:90:522:469:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:under domestic law, as indicated by the restrictions of the obligation characteristics.
53:2178:115285:26:13:90:522:443:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:The final non-trivial aspect relates to the deliverable obligation categories and the
53:2179:115370:13:14:90:522:430:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:associated characteristics.  While in the presence of Credit Events for SWESs, bonds
53:2180:115454:14:14:90:522:416:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:or loans are deliverable during the auction settlement process, SEES contracts allow
53:2181:115538:14:14:90:522:402:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:only for bonds to be delivered. Several restrictions apply to the deliverable obligations,
53:2182:115628:14:14:90:522:388:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:such that for SWESs they have to be denominated in a specified currency (i.e., the
53:2183:115710:14:14:90:522:374:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:Euro or the currencies of Canada,  Japan,  Switzerland,  the UK, or the USA), they
53:2184:115792:14:14:90:522:360:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:must be non-contingent, non-bearer and transferable, limited to a maximum maturity
53:2185:115874:14:14:90:522:346:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:of 30 years, and loans must be assignable and consent is required.  SEES contracts
53:2186:115956:14:14:90:522:332:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:exclude these restrictions on loans and the maximum deliverable maturity, but impose
53:2187:116040:14:14:90:522:318:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:the  additional  constraints  that  the  obligation  cannot  be  subordinated,  and  issued
53:2188:116131:14:48:90:274:304:12:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f18:C:domestically or under domestic law.
53:2189:116166:48:38:90:459:256:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:B    Term structure of quanto spreads in the iid case
